الذي لا أب له ففاتت العفة، والثالثة: رجل قذف رجلاً قد وطئ في غير ملكه فلا يحد؛ لفوات العفة عن المقذوف وقاذفه صادق، الرابعة: رجل وطئ أمة مشتركة بينه وبين غيره فلا يحد؛ لأن الحرمة فيها من وجه دون وجه، في غير الملك من كل وجه كالأجنبية، أو من وجه كالأمة المشتركة، أو في الملك والحرمة مؤبدة كأمته التي حرمت عليه بالرضاع أو بالمصاهرة بشرط أن يكون ثبوت حرمتها بالإجماع أو بالخبر المشهور يسقط الإحصان عند أبي حنيفة، حتى لا يحد قاذفه، ومن الحرمة لعينه جارية ابنه، والمنكوحة نكاحاً فاسداً، والأمة المستحقة، والمكرهة على الزنا، ومنها: إذا زنى بامرأة ثم اشترى أمها أو بنتها، أو تزوجها فوطئها. ومنها: إذا زنى فوطئهما أو إحداهما، أو وطئ مكاتبته أو الحائض أو امرأته التي ظاهر منها أو المحرمة بالإيلاء، كل ذلك لا يسقط الإحصان. ولو نظر إلى فرج امرأة أو لمسها بشهوة ثم تزوج أمها أو بنتها أو اشتراها فوطئها، لا يسقط إحصانه عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن الحرمة لم ينعقد عليها إجماع خلافاً لهما، والمسألة الخامسة: رجل قذف رجلاً قد زنى في حالة كفره ثم أسلم فلا يحد قاذفه؛ لأنه صادق فيه؛ لأن الزنا يتحقق من الكافر حربياً كان أو ذمياً في دار الإسلام أو في دار الحرب فيسقط به إحصانه، والسادسة: رجل قذف مكاتباً مات وترك مالاً يفي ببدل الكتابة لا يحد القاذف؛ لأن الحد إنما يجب بقذف الحرة، وفي حرية هذا المكاتب تمكن الشبهة؛ لأن الصحابة اختلفوا في موته حراً أو عبداً، فأورث شبهة، والإحصان لم يكن ثابتاً فلا يثبت بالشك. (عيني، فتح) ولدها: سواء كان الولد حياً أو ميتاً. (عيني) أو لاعنت : بأن كان اللعان بينهما وبين زوجها بنفي ولد. (عيني) عن وفاء: أي مال يفي ببدل الكتابة. (ط) وحد قاذف واطئ أمة إلخ أي يحد القاذف في هذه المسائل الأربع؛ لأن لكل منها صورة الوطء الحرام لغيره، وقد قلنا: إن الوطء إن كان حراماً لغيره لا يوجب سقوط الإحصان، فإذا لم يسقط الإحصان بقي المقذوف محصنا، فيحد قاذفه الأولى : رجل قذف رجلاً قد وطئ أمته المجوسية، فعلى القاذف الحد؛ لأن وطئها حرام، لكن حرمته لغيره، وهو كونها مجوسية، والثانية: رجل قذف رجلاً قد وطئ زوجته أو أمته في حالة الحيض فيحد القاذف؛ لأن حرمة وطء الحائض موقتة إلى زمان الطهر، فكانت الحرمة لغيره. والثالثة: رجل قذف رجلاً قد وطئ مكاتبته، فيحد القاذف عند الطرفين، وعن أبي يوسف: أن وطء المكاتبة يسقط الإحصان وبه قال زفر؛ لأن الملك زائل في حق الوطء، ولهذا لزمه العقر بوطئها، قلنا: ملك المولى فيها ثابت من كل وجه، ولهذا جاز عتقها عن كفارة اليمين ووجوب العقر لا ينافي الحل، فكيف ينافي الشبهة، =
Slandering a woman etc. 'Man' is a relative pronoun, 'qadhafa' with its conjuncts is the relative clause, and the sentence is a subject. His statement: 'he is not punished' is the predicate. It comprises six issues: First: a man slanders a woman and she has a child whose father is unknown; he is not punished due to the existence of an indication of zina. Second: a man slanders a woman who performed li'an due to a child, i.e., because of the denial of the child, she performed li'an with her husband. It is restricted to a child because if she performs li'an without a child (i.e., due to slander), then her slanderer is punished due to the absence of an indication of zina. So the slanderer of the woman who performed li'an due to denial of a child is not punished because there is an indication of zina in her, which is giving birth to a child with no father, so she loses chastity. Third: a man slanders a man who has had intercourse in something not his property; he is not punished because chastity is lost from the accused and his accuser is truthful. Fourth: a man has intercourse with a joint slave-girl between him and another; he is not punished because the prohibition is from one aspect not another, so chastity is absent. Fifth: a man slanders a man who committed zina while a disbeliever then became Muslim; he is not punished because he is truthful in it, since zina is verified from a disbeliever, whether a harbi or a dhimmi in Dar al-Islam or Dar al-Harb, so his chastity is thus lost. Sixth: a man slanders a mukatib who died leaving wealth that suffices for the kitaba; the slanderer is not punished because the hadd is only obligatory by slandering a free woman, and in the freedom of this mukatib there is a doubt because the Companions differed on whether he dies free or a slave, which became a doubt, and chastity was not established so it is not established by doubt. (Ayni, Fath) 'Her child': whether the child is alive or dead. (Ayni) 'Or performed li'an': i.e., there was li'an between her and her husband due to denying a child. (Ayni) 'From suffices': i.e., wealth that suffices for the kitaba. (T) 'And the hadd of the slanderer of one who had intercourse with a slave-girl etc.': i.e., the slanderer is punished in these four issues because each of them is a case of intercourse that is forbidden due to an external factor. We have said that if intercourse is forbidden due to an external factor, it does not cause the loss of chastity. So when chastity is not lost, the accused remains chaste (muhsan), so his slanderer is punished. The first: a man slanders a man who has had intercourse with his Magian slave-girl; the slanderer is liable for hadd because his intercourse is forbidden, but the prohibition is due to an external factor, namely her being Magian. The second: a man slanders a man who has had intercourse with his wife or his slave-girl during menstruation; the slanderer is punished because the prohibition of intercourse with a menstruating woman is temporary until purity, so the prohibition is due to an external factor. The third: a man slanders a man who has had intercourse with his mukataba; the slanderer is punished according to both parties. From Abu Yusuf: that intercourse with a mukataba does not nullify chastity, and Zufar said the same because ownership is removed with respect to intercourse, and for this reason, if he has intercourse with her, he must pay the 'aqr (compensation). We say: the master's ownership in her is established from every aspect, so her manumission is valid for the expiation of an oath, and the obligation of 'aqr does not contradict permissibility, so how could it contradict doubt?
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage details six situations where a person who slanders (qadhf) another is not subject to the hadd punishment of 80 lashes, because the accused person exhibits 'indications of zina' (amarat al-zina) that undermine their claim to chastity (ihsan). The six cases are: (1) a woman with a child of unknown father, (2) a woman who performed li'an due to a child, (3) a man who had intercourse in non-owned property (like an unrelated woman), (4) a man who had intercourse with a jointly-owned slave-girl, (5) a man who committed zina while a disbeliever and later converted to Islam, and (6) a mukatib (a slave under contract of manumission) who dies leaving enough to pay his kitaba. In each case, the slanderer is not punished because the accused lacks full chastity. The passage then explains a general principle: if a person engages in intercourse that is inherently forbidden (haram li-aynihi), such as zina with an unrelated woman or incest, then the slanderer is not punished because the accused's chastity is lost. However, if the intercourse is forbidden due to an external factor (haram li-ghayrihi), such as with a Magian slave-girl (because she is a fire-worshipper) or with a menstruating wife, then the slanderer is punished because the accused remains chaste. The commentators note that Imam Abu Hanifa considers some types of prohibition as inherent, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ on some points. For example, regarding intercourse with a mukataba, Abu Yusuf and Zufar hold that it nullifies chastity, but the relied-upon position is that it does not.

Key Terms
أمارة الزنا (amarat al-zina): An indication or strong likelihood of zina, such as a woman having a child without a known husband, which removes the presumption of chastity.
الإحصان (al-ihsan): Chastity; a quality that protects a person from being lawfully subjected to the hadd of qadhf. It is lost through engaging in unlawful intercourse or through clear indications of zina.
مكاتب (mukatib): A slave who has contracted with his master for manumission in exchange for payments. His status is between slave and free, creating doubt (shubha) regarding his freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A man who slanders a woman who gave birth to a child out of wedlock.
B) A man who slanders a man who had intercourse with his Magian slave-girl.
C) A man who slanders a man who had intercourse with his menstruating wife.
D) A man who slanders a man who had intercourse with his own slave-girl (owned solely by him) during her menses.

Key Takeaway
A slanderer is only punished if the accused is truly chaste (muhsan); indications of zina or inherently forbidden intercourse remove that chastity.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate

The Core Principle: Ihsan and the Haram Li-Aynihi vs Li-Ghayrihi Distinction
Establishes the core principle and lists examples of inherently forbidden intercourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that determines when slandering a person incurs hadd, and identify whether a given act of intercourse drops ihsan or not.

Core Idea
Slandering one who committed inherently forbidden intercourse (haram li-aynihi) does not incur hadd; slandering one who committed intercourse forbidden for external reasons (haram li-ghayrihi) does.

This lesson introduces the foundational rule for Hadd al-Qadhf. The key is whether the slandered person's act of intercourse was forbidden in itself or due to an external factor. The text begins by stating the principle and then provides a range of examples of intercourse that is inherently forbidden, all of which drop ihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is slandering (qadhf) a person by accusing them of zina. The ruling depends on the slandered person's state: if they are muhsan, the slanderer incurs hadd; if not, no hadd.
2
Define ihsan in this context
Ihsan here means the slandered person is free, adult, Muslim, and has never committed inherently forbidden intercourse. If they have committed such intercourse, they are not muhsan.
Other schools define ihsan differently for zina hadd.
3
Distinguish haram li-aynihi from haram li-ghayrihi
Haram li-aynihi is intercourse that is forbidden regardless of the person (e.g., zina, incest). Haram li-ghayrihi is intercourse that is forbidden due to an external circumstance (e.g., menstruation, being married to another).
The text provides examples of haram li-aynihi.
4
Apply the principle to a simple scenario
Given a person who committed zina with a foreign woman (haram li-aynihi), slandering him does not incur hadd. If a person had intercourse with his menstruating wife (haram li-ghayrihi), slandering him incurs hadd.
Practice with the checkpoint.

كتاب الحدود باب حد القذف ولدها، أو لاعنت بولد، أو رجلاً وطئ في غير ملكه أو أمة مشتركة أو مسلماً أي أو قذف امرأة أي أو قذف رجلاً كأمة الغير أي أو وطئ أو قذف رجلاً مسلماً زنى في كفره، أو مكاتباً مات عن وفاء لا يحدّ، وحدّ قاذف واطئ أمة مجوسية أي أو قذف مكاتبا أي القاذف في الصور الست والأصل فيه أن كل من وطئ وطئاً حراماً لعينه لا يحد قاذفه وإن كان الوطء حراماً لغيره حد قاذفه، فالوطء في غير الملك من كل وجه كالأجنبية، أو من وجه كالأمة المشتركة، أو في الملك والحرمة مؤبدة كأمته التي حرمت عليه بالرضاع أو بالمصاهرة بشرط أن يكون ثبوت حرمتها بالإجماع أو بالخبر المشهور يسقط الإحصان عند أبي حنيفة، حتى لا يحد قاذفه، ومن الحرمة لعينه جارية ابنه، والمنكوحة نكاحاً فاسداً، والأمة المستحقة، والمكرهة على الزنا، ومنها: إذا زنى بامرأة ثم اشترى أمها أو بنتها، أو تزوجها فوطئها. ومنها: إذا زنى أبوه بامرأة ثم تزوجها الابن أو اشتراها فوطئها، فإن الحرمة فيها ثابتة بنص قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تَنْكِحُوا مَا نَكَحَ آبَاؤُكُمْ (النساء: ۲۲)، ومنها: إذا تزوج محارمه ودخل بها، أو جمع بين الأختين أو غيرهما من المحارم، أو تزوج أمة على حرة، فوطئها كل ذلك يسقط الإحصان، وإن كانت الحرمة غير مؤبدة كأمة المتزوجة والمجوسية لا يسقط أحصانه بوطئها، وكذا إذا اشترى أمة شراء فاسداً، أو كان في ملكه أمتان أختان، فوطئهما أو إحداهما، أو وطئ مكاتبته أو الحائض أو امرأته التي ظاهر منها أو المحرمة بالإيلاء، كل ذلك لا يسقط الإحصان. ولو نظر إلى فرج امرأة أو لمسها بشهوة ثم تزوج أمها أو بنتها أو اشتراها فوطئها، لا يسقط إحصانه عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن الحرمة لم ينعقد عليها إجماع خلافاً لهما، والمسألة الخامسة: رجل قذف رجلاً قد زنى في حالة كفره ثم أسلم فلا يحد قاذفه؛ لأنه صادق فيه؛ لأن الزنا يتحقق من الكافر حربياً كان أو ذمياً في دار الإسلام أو في دار الحرب فيسقط به إحصانه، والسادسة: رجل قذف مكاتباً مات وترك مالاً يفي ببدل الكتابة لا يحد القاذف؛ لأن الحد إنما يجب بقذف الحرة، وفي حرية هذا المكاتب تمكن الشبهة؛ لأن الصحابة اختلفوا في موته حراً أو عبداً، فأورث شبهة، والإحصان لم يكن ثابتاً فلا يثبت بالشك. (عيني، فتح) ولدها: سواء كان الولد حياً أو ميتاً. (عيني) أو لاعنت : بأن كان اللعان بينهما وبين زوجها بنفي ولد. (عيني) عن وفاء: أي مال يفي ببدل الكتابة. (ط) وحد قاذف واطئ أمة إلخ أي يحد القاذف في هذه المسائل الأربع؛ لأن لكل منها صورة الوطء الحرام لغيره، وقد قلنا: إن الوطء إن كان حراماً لغيره لا يوجب سقوط الإحصان، فإذا لم يسقط الإحصان بقي المقذوف محصناً، فيحد قاذفه الأولى : رجل قذف رجلاً قد وطئ أمته المجوسية، فعلى القاذف الحد؛ لأن وطئها حرام، لكن حرمته لغيره، وهو كونها مجوسية، والثانية: رجل قذف رجلاً قد وطئ زوجته أو أمته في حالة الحيض فيحد القاذف؛ لأن حرمة وطء الحائض موقتة إلى زمان الطهر، فكانت الحرمة لغيره. والثالثة: رجل قذف رجلاً قد وطئ مكاتبته، فيحد القاذف عند الطرفين، وعن أبي يوسف: أن وطء المكاتبة يسقط الإحصان وبه قال زفر؛ لأن الملك زائل في حق الوطء، ولهذا لزمه العقر بوطئها، قلنا: ملك المولى فيها ثابت من كل وجه، ولهذا جاز عتقها عن كفارة اليمين ووجوب العقر لا ينافي الحل، فكيف ينافي الشبهة، الرابعة: رجل قذف مسلماً قد نكح أمه حال كونه كافراً يحد القاذف عند أبي حنيفة وقالا لا يحد وهذا مبني على أن نكاحهم بالمحارم صحيح فيما بينهم عنده، وعندهما فاسد، وقد مر في النكاح. (مستخلص، عيني) ومكاتبة: أي حد قاذف واطئ مكاتبته؛ لأن ملكه ثابت فيها خلافاً لأبي يوسف وزفر. (عيني، مستخلص) في كفره: أي في حال كفره أو غير الأم من المحارم (ط) ومستأمن قذف مسلماً: ولا يحد للزنا والسرقة، والذمي يحد في الكل. (عيني) بالرفع عطف على قوله: قاذف أي وحد مستأمن قذف مسلماً في دار الإسلام، وكان أبو حنيفة يقول أولاً : لا يحد؛ لأن الغالب فيه حق الله، فصار كسائر الحدود، ثم رجع إلى ما ذكر هنا، ووجهه أن في القذف حق العبد، وقد التزم المستأمن استيفاء حقوق العباد. والحاصل: أن حد القذف يجب عليه اتفاقاً، وحد الخمر لا يجب عليه اتفاقاً، ولا يجب حد الزنا والسرقة، خلافاً لأبي يوسف، وأما الذمي فيجب عليه جميع الحدود اتفاقاً إلا حد الخمر، والصحيح الحد بالسكر فيها أيضاً، وإذا اعتقدوا حرمة الخمر كانوا كالمسلمين. ثم إذا حد المسلم في قذف تسقط شهادته وإن تاب؛ لأن رد شهادته من تمام حده؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً أَبَداً (النور: ٤) وإذا حد الكافر في قذف لم تجز شهادته على أهل الذمة، فإن أسلم قبلت شهادته عليهم وعلى المسلمين؛ لأن هذه الشهادة استفادها بالإسلام فكانت غير مردودة، والعبد إذا حد في قذف ثم عتق لم تقبل شهادته. (مستخلص، فتح) ومن قذف مراراً رجلاً واحداً أو متعدداً. (ط، عيني) فهو لكله: أي الحد الذي حد به المجرم يكون لكل قذف مراراً ولكل زنا مراراً ولكل شرب مراراً لحصول المقصود وللتداخل في العقوبات بخلاف ما إذا زنى وقذف وشرب حيث يحد لكل واحد على حدة؛ لعدم حصول المقصود بالبعض؛ لاختلاف الأسباب والأغراض، فإن المقصود من حد الزنا صيانة الأنساب ومن حد القذف صيانة الأعراض ومن حد الشرب صيانة العقول فلا يحصل بكل جنس إلا ما قصد لشرعه ولا يوالي بين الحدود خيفة الهلاك، بل ينتظر حتى يبرأ من الأول. فعلى هذا لو جلد للقذف إلا سوطاً ثم قذف آخر في المجلس، فإنه يتم الأول، ولا شيء عليه للثاني للتداخل. ولو ضرب للزنا أو للشرب بعض الحد فهرب ثم زنى أو شرب ثانياً حد حداً مستأنفاً، وقال الشافعي له: إن حد القذف لا يتداخل إلا إذا قذف جماعة بكلمة واحدة أو قذف واحداً بزنا، ثم قذفه بزنا آخر، لا يتداخل الحد بل يجب لكل قذف حد. رمز الحقائق: ۳۹۷/۱] (فتح)
The Book of Hudud, Chapter of Hadd al-Qadhf. And [if the slandered person is] her child, or she engaged in li'an with a child, or a man who had intercourse outside his ownership, or a jointly owned slave girl, or a Muslim [who committed zina] while in kufr, or a mukatib who died and left sufficient wealth, [then the slanderer] is not flogged. And the slanderer of one who had intercourse with a Magian slave girl is flogged. The principle is: whoever has intercourse that is forbidden in itself, his slanderer is not flogged; but if the intercourse is forbidden due to an external factor, his slanderer is flogged. Intercourse outside ownership entirely, like with a foreign woman, or partially, like with a jointly owned slave girl, or something owned with perpetual prohibition, like his slave woman who became forbidden to him through fosterage or marriage relation, provided that the prohibition is established by consensus or by widely reported report, drops ihsan according to Abu Hanifa, so his slanderer is not flogged. Examples of inherently forbidden intercourse: his son's slave girl, one married with a corrupt contract, a claimed slave girl, and one forced into zina. Also, if a man committed zina with a woman then bought her mother or daughter, or married her and had intercourse – all these drop ihsan. If his father committed zina with a woman then the son married her or bought her and had intercourse – the prohibition is established by the text of the Quran: 'Do not marry what your fathers married' (al-Nisa: 22). If he married his mahrams and consummated, or brought together two sisters or other mahrams, or married a slave girl over a free woman and consummated – all drop ihsan. But if the prohibition is not perpetual, like a married slave girl or a Magian woman, ihsan is not dropped by intercourse with her. Similarly, if he bought a slave girl with a corrupt purchase, or owned two sisters as slave girls and had intercourse with both or one, or had intercourse with his mukatibah, or a menstruating woman, or his wife from whom he made dhihar, or one forbidden by ila – none of this drops ihsan. If he looked at a woman's private part or touched it with desire, then married her mother or daughter or bought her and had intercourse – it does not drop his ihsan according to Abu Hanifa, because the prohibition is not established by consensus; contrary to the two companions. The fifth case: a man slanders a man who committed zina while in kufr then converted; the slanderer is not flogged because he is truthful; for zina is indeed committed by a disbeliever, whether harbi or dhimmi, in Dar al-Islam or Dar al-Harb, so it drops his ihsan. The sixth case: a man slanders a mukatib who died leaving wealth sufficient to cover the kitabah; the slanderer is not flogged because the hadd is only obligatory for slandering a free woman, and in the freedom of this mukatib there is a doubt, since the Companions differed on whether he dies free or slave, thus creating a doubt, and ihsan was not established, so it is not established by doubt. (Ayni, Fath) 'Her child': whether the child is alive or dead. (Ayni) 'She engaged in li'an': meaning that li'an occurred between her and her husband denying the child. (Ayni) 'Leaving wealth': meaning wealth that covers the kitabah. (T) 'And the slanderer of one who had intercourse with a slave woman etc.': meaning the slanderer is flogged in these four cases, because each involves the form of intercourse that is forbidden due to an external factor, and we have said that if intercourse is forbidden due to an external factor, it does not cause ihsan to fall, so ihsan remains and the slanderer is flogged. First case: a man slanders a man who had intercourse with his Magian slave girl; the slanderer incurs hadd, because intercourse with her is forbidden, but its prohibition is due to an external factor – her being Magian. Second case: a man slanders a man who had intercourse with his wife or his slave girl while she was menstruating; the slanderer is flogged, because the prohibition of intercourse with a menstruating woman is temporary until purity, so the prohibition is due to an external factor. Third case: a man slanders a man who had intercourse with his mukatibah; the slanderer is flogged according to both [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad]; and from Abu Yusuf: intercourse with the mukatibah drops ihsan, and Zafar also said this, because ownership is nullified with respect to intercourse, therefore he must pay the dower for intercourse with her. We say: the master's ownership of her is established from all aspects, therefore it is permissible to free her as expiation for an oath, and the obligation of dower does not contradict permissibility, so how could it create a doubt? Fourth case: a man slanders a Muslim who married his mother while he was in kufr; the slanderer is flogged according to Abu Hanifa, but both [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said he is not flogged. This is based on whether their marriage to mahrams is valid among them according to him, but invalid according to them, and this has passed in the Book of Nikah. (Mustakhlas, Ayni) 'Mukatibah': meaning the slanderer of one who had intercourse with his mukatibah is flogged, because his ownership of her is established, contrary to Abu Yusuf and Zafar. (Ayni, Mustakhlas) 'While in his kufr': meaning while [the slandered person] was in kufr, or other than the mother from the mahrams. (T) 'And a musta'man who slanders a Muslim': he is not flogged for zina and theft, but the dhimmi is flogged in all [such cases]. (Ayni) In the nominative, it is coordinated with 'slanderer', meaning 'the hadd of a musta'man who slanders a Muslim in Dar al-Islam'. Abu Hanifa initially used to say: he is not flogged, because the right of Allah predominates, so it is like other hudud; then he retracted to what is mentioned here, and the reasoning is that in slander there is the right of the slave, and the musta'man has pledged to fulfill the rights of the subjects. The conclusion: slander hadd is obligatory on him by agreement; khamr hadd is not obligatory on him by agreement; and zina and theft hadd are not obligatory on him, contrary to Abu Yusuf. As for the dhimmi, all hudud are obligatory on him by agreement except khamr hadd; but the correct view is that hadd for intoxication is also [obligatory] if they believe khamr is forbidden, then they are like Muslims. Then, if a Muslim is flogged for slander, his testimony is rejected even if he repents, because rejection of his testimony is part of his hadd; due to the Quranic verse: 'And never accept their testimony' (al-Nur: 4). If a disbeliever is flogged for slander, his testimony against the dhimmis is not permissible; but if he converts, his testimony against them and against Muslims is accepted, because this testimony is acquired through Islam, so it is not rejected. And a slave who is flogged for slander and then freed – his testimony is not accepted. (Mustakhlas, Fath) 'Who slanders repeatedly': whether one man or many. (T, Ayni) 'So the flogging is for all': meaning the hadd that the criminal was flogged with is for each slander repeatedly, and for each zina repeatedly, and for each drinking repeatedly, because the purpose is achieved and punishments merge. Unlike if he committed zina, slander, and drinking – he is flogged separately for each, because the purpose is not achieved by some, due to different causes and objectives; the purpose of zina hadd is preservation of lineage, of slander hadd is preservation of honor, of drinking hadd is preservation of intellect; each type only achieves what is intended by its legislation. And multiple punishments [of different types] should not be combined for fear of destruction, but rather one waits until the first recovers. According to this, if he was flogged for slander except one lash, then he slanders another in the same session, the first is completed and nothing is imposed for the second due to merging. If he was struck some of the hadd for zina or drinking and then fled, and then committed zina or drinking a second time, he is flogged a fresh hadd. Al-Shafi'i said: The hadd for slander does not merge; if one slanders a group with one word, or slanders one person for zina then slanders him for another zina, the hadd does not merge, and a separate hadd is obligatory for each slander. Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 397/1 (Fath)
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq opens the chapter on Hadd al-Qadhf (the slander punishment). It is a ruling statement with extensive commentary and inter-madhhab disputes. The author begins by listing several scenarios where slandering a person does not incur hadd: slandering a child born from zina, a woman who engaged in li'an, a man who had intercourse with a woman outside his ownership, a jointly owned slave girl, a Muslim who committed zina while a disbeliever, or a mukatib who died with sufficient wealth. Then it states the opposite: slandering one who had intercourse with a Magian slave girl does incur hadd.

The core principle (al-asl) is then established: if the slandered person committed intercourse that is forbidden in itself (haram li-aynihi), slandering him does not incur hadd; if the intercourse is forbidden due to an external factor (haram li-ghayrihi), slandering him incurs hadd. The reason is that ihsan (being in a state that makes slander punishable by hadd) is dropped by committing inherently forbidden intercourse, but not by intercourse forbidden for an extraneous reason.

The text then provides detailed examples of both categories. Forbidden in itself: intercourse outside ownership entirely (like with a foreign woman), partially (like a jointly owned slave), or with a woman perpetually forbidden due to fosterage or marriage, provided the prohibition is established by ijma' or widely reported hadith – according to Abu Hanifa, this drops ihsan. Also included: his son's slave girl, a marriage with a corrupt contract, a claimed slave girl, forced zina, and cases where zina leads to subsequent marriage or purchase of relatives (e.g., zina with a woman then buying her mother creates a perpetual prohibition by Quranic text). Other examples: marrying mahrams and consummating, bringing together two sisters, or marrying a slave over a free woman.

Conversely, intercourse that is forbidden due to an external factor includes: a married slave girl (married to another), a Magian woman (disbeliever), a slave bought with a corrupt contract, having intercourse with two sisters owned as slaves, a mukatibah (slave on a contract of freedom), a menstruating woman, a wife from whom dhihar was made, or a woman forbidden by ila. Also, looking or touching with desire then marrying the woman's mother/daughter does not drop ihsan according to Abu Hanifa (contrary to the two companions) because the prohibition is not established by consensus.

Two specific cases are then discussed: fifth case – slandering a convert who committed zina while a disbeliever: no hadd because the statement is true; zina by a disbeliever is real; it drops ihsan. Sixth case – slandering a mukatib who died with sufficient wealth: no hadd due to doubt about his freedom (since Companions differed on whether a mukatib dying with wealth dies free or slave).

The commentary then explains four cases where hadd IS imposed: 1) intercourse with a Magian slave girl, 2) intercourse with a menstruating woman, 3) intercourse with a mukatibah (here there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf and Zafar say it drops ihsan, but the majority say it does not), 4) a Muslim who married his mother while a disbeliever (Abu Hanifa says hadd is imposed because he considers such marriages valid among disbelievers; the two companions say they are invalid, so no hadd).

A separate ruling concerns a musta'man (non-Muslim with temporary security) who slanders a Muslim in Dar al-Islam: Initially, Abu Hanifa said no hadd because it is a right of Allah, but retracted; the relied-upon view is that slander hadd is obligatory because it involves right of the slave, and the musta'man has pledged to uphold such rights. However, for zina, theft, and drinking, hadd is not obligatory on the musta'man (contrary to Abu Yusuf). For a dhimmi, all hudud apply except drinking if they do not believe it is forbidden; if they do, then hadd applies.

Finally, the passage discusses the effect of hadd on testimony: a Muslim flogged for slander has his testimony rejected forever, even after repentance, based on Quran 24:4. If a disbeliever (dhimmi) is flogged for slander, his testimony against dhimmis is not accepted, but if he converts, it becomes accepted. A slave flogged for slander who later is freed still has his testimony rejected.

Regarding multiple crimes: if a person slanders repeatedly, or commits zina repeatedly, or drinks repeatedly, one hadd suffices for all because the punishment merges (tadakhul) when the same purpose is achieved. But if he commits different crimes (zina, slander, drinking), each requires a separate hadd because each serves a different purpose. However, within the same crime, if he is punished partway and then repeats, the second act does not require a new hadd if it is of the same type (e.g., slander after partial flogging for slander – the first is completed, no new hadd). But for zina or drinking, if he flees after partial flogging and then repeats, he must be flogged anew. This contrasts with the Shafi'i position, which does not allow merging for slander except in very specific circumstances.

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsan): In the context of hadd al-qadhf, ihsan is the condition of being a free, adult, Muslim who has never committed inherently forbidden intercourse. Being muhsan means slandering such a person incurs hadd.
قذف (qadhf): Accusing a chaste person of zina without four witnesses. It is a crime punishable by 80 lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following acts of intercourse would drop ihsan according to the Hanafi school, such that slandering the perpetrator does not incur hadd?
A) Intercourse with a menstruating wife
B) Intercourse with a foreign woman (zina)
C) Intercourse with a married slave girl
D) Intercourse with one's own wife during the day in Ramadan

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between inherently forbidden intercourse (haram li-aynihi), which drops ihsan, and externally forbidden intercourse (haram li-ghayrihi), which does not – this determines whether slander incurs hadd.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Qadhf for a Muslim Who Married His Mother While Kafir
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qadhf hadd for a specific case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on qadhf hadd when the victim married a mahram while kafir, explain the basis of each position, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A marriage to a mahram in kufr is valid per Abu Hanifa, making the victim muhsan and the qadhif liable for hadd.

This lesson explores a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: when a Muslim who previously married his mother while a kafir is accused of zina, does the accuser receive the hadd penalty? The answer hinges on whether that marriage is considered valid among kuffar. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differed on this point, and the ruling has significant practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the dispute
The passage presents a specific scenario: a Muslim man, who during his time as a kafir married his own mother (a mahram), is later accused of zina by another Muslim. The question is whether the accuser (qadhif) incurs the hadd penalty.
Note the victim is now Muslim, but the marriage occurred in kufr.
2
State each position
Abu Hanifa holds that the qadhif receives hadd. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the qadhif does not receive hadd, only ta'zir.
The dispute is confined within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the basis of each position
The disagreement rests on whether a marriage to a mahram (like one's mother) is valid among kuffar. Abu Hanifa considers such marriages valid among them, so the victim is muhsan. The Sahibayn consider them inherently invalid (fasid), so the victim is not muhsan.
This is a rational (aqli) proof, not directly from text.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
If Abu Hanifa's view is followed, the qadhif receives 80 lashes and his testimony is permanently rejected. If the Sahibayn's view is followed, only ta'zir is given and testimony is not rejected.
The practical consequence is significant for the qadhif's rights.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as indicated by the structure of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and subsequent commentaries.
References to the nikah chapter confirm the issue was settled.

ومسلم نكح أمه في كفره، الرابعة: رجل قذف مسلماً قد نكح أمه حال كونه كافراً يحد القاذف عند أبي حنيفة وقالا لا يحد وهذا مبني على أن نكاحهم بالمحارم صحيح فيما بينهم عنده، وعندهما فاسد، وقد مر في النكاح. (مستخلص، عيني)
And a Muslim who married his mother in his state of kufr, the fourth: a man who qadhf a Muslim who had married his mother while being a kafir, the qadhif is hadded according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Sahibayn) said he is not hadded. This is based on the fact that their marriage to mahrams is valid among them according to him, and according to them it is fasid. It has passed in the nikah chapter. (Mustakhlas, Ayni)
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the hadd punishment for qadhf when the victim (the one accused of zina) is a Muslim who, during his time as a kafir, married his mother (a mahram). The ruling turns on the validity of that marriage in kufr. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the marriage of kuffar to mahrams is valid among them; thus, the victim is considered muhsan (protected) in the sense that he was in a valid marriage, and therefore the qadhif is liable for hadd al-qadhf. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) hold that such a marriage is invalid (fasid) because it is inherently prohibited, so the victim is not muhsan, and the qadhif only receives ta'zir. The author references that this issue was discussed earlier in the marriage chapter. The position of Abu Hanifa is the relied-upon position in the school as per the weight of the matn.

Key Terms
محصن (muhsan): A person who is free, Muslim, and has had valid sexual intercourse in a valid marriage; required for hadd al-qadhf.
قذف (qadhf): Accusation of zina against a muhsan person without four witnesses.
فاسد (fasid): Invalid due to a defect in the contract; for marriage, a fasid marriage does not produce legal effects like muhsan status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The validity of a marriage contracted in kufr is determined by the laws of the kuffar; Abu Hanifa holds it valid even if the spouses are mahram, thus the qadhif incurs hadd.

Hadd al-Qadhf for a Musta'min: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on musta'min's liability for hadd al-qadhf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on which hudud apply to a musta'min, explain the rationale for applying hadd al-qadhf but not zina and theft, and identify the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A musta'min is hadded for qadhf (private right) but not zina or theft (public rights).

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the application of hudud punishments to a musta'min—a non-Muslim granted safe conduct. While one might assume the musta'min is exempt from all hadd punishments, the Hanafi school distinguishes between offenses involving private rights and those involving purely public rights. The ruling on qadhf, which involves a servant's right, is particularly instructive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the settled Hanafi position
State that a musta'min committing qadhf against a Muslim is subject to the hadd punishment by consensus among the Hanafi imams (after Abu Hanifa's retraction).
This is the mufta bihi.
2
Trace Abu Hanifa's initial view and retraction
Abu Hanifa initially held that no hadd applies because the hadd is predominantly a right of Allah. He later retracted and ruled that the hadd is wajib because qadhf involves a private right (haqq al-'abd).
This change is called al-ruju'.
3
Analyze the rationale
The justification is that the musta'min, by accepting safe conduct, has committed to respecting the rights of Muslims. Qadhf violates a private right (honor), so the hadd is imposed. Zina and theft are primarily rights of Allah, so they are not imposed.
Distinction between haqq Allah and haqq al-'abd.
4
Note Abu Yusuf's disagreement
Abu Yusuf held that a musta'min should also be hadded for zina and theft, likely viewing all hudud as equally binding on non-Muslims in the Islamic state.
This is a minority view within the Hanafi school.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is that the hadd of qadhf is wajib on the musta'min, while the hadd of zina and theft are not. The practical consequence is that a musta'min who commits zina or theft is punished by ta'zir, not hadd.
This is based on the later view of Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومستأمن قذف مسلماً: [ولا يحد للزنا والسرقة، والذمي يحد في الكل. (عيني) بالرفع عطف على قوله: قاذف" أي وحد مستأمن قذف مسلماً في دار الإسلام، وكان أبو حنيفة يقول أولاً : لا يحد؛ لأن الغالب فيه حق الله، فصار كسائر الحدود، ثم رجع إلى ما ذكر هنا، ووجهه أن في القذف حق العبد، وقد التزم المستأمن استيفاء حقوق العباد. والحاصل: أن حد القذف يجب عليه اتفاقاً، وحد الخمر لا يجب عليه اتفاقاً، ولا يجب حد الزنا والسرقة، خلافاً لأبي يوسف، وأما الذمي فيجب عليه جميع الحدود اتفاقاً إلا حد الخمر، والصحيح الحد بالسكر فيها أيضاً، وإذا اعتقدوا حرمة الخمر كانوا كالمسلمين.]
And a musta'min who qadhf a Muslim: [He is not hadded for zina and theft, but the dhimmi is hadded for all. (Ayni) With rafa' (nominative) as an 'atf on his saying 'qadhif': meaning the hadd of a musta'min who qadhf a Muslim in the abode of Islam. Abu Hanifa initially said he is not hadded because the predominant (element) is the right of Allah, so it became like other hudud. Then he returned to what is mentioned here, and its justification is that in qadhf there is a right of the servant, and the musta'min has committed to fulfilling the rights of the subjects. The bottom line: the hadd of qadhf is obligatory on him by agreement, the hadd of wine is not obligatory on him by agreement, and the hadd of zina and theft are not obligatory, contrary to Abu Yusuf. As for the dhimmi, all hudud are obligatory on him by agreement except the hadd of wine, and the correct view is that he is hadded for intoxication as well, and if they believe that wine is haram, they are like Muslims.]
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage discusses the liability of a musta'min (a non-Muslim given safe conduct in the Islamic state) for hudud punishments. The rule is that a musta'min is subject to the hadd of qadhf by consensus of the Hanafi imams, because qadhf involves a private right (of the accuser) that the musta'min has agreed to respect. However, he is not hadded for zina or theft (which are primarily public rights), unlike a dhimmi who is liable for all hudud except the hadd for drinking wine (and even that, if he believes it is haram). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa initially held that the musta'min is not hadded for qadhf either, because the hadd is predominantly a right of Allah, but then he retracted and held the view that the musta'min is hadded. Abu Yusuf disagreed on some points regarding zina and theft. The relied-upon position is that the hadd of qadhf is wajib on the musta'min, while the hadd of zina and theft are not.

Key Terms
مستأمن (musta'min): A non-Muslim who enters the Islamic state with a temporary safe conduct (aman).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadd is a musta'min liable for according to all Hanafi imams?
A) Hadd al-zina
B) Hadd al-sariqa
C) Hadd al-qadhf
D) Hadd al-shurb

Key Takeaway
A musta'min is subject to hadd al-qadhf because it involves a private right, but not to hadd for zina or theft, which are predominantly rights of Allah.

The Principle of Tadakhul in Hudud Punishments
Rule on overlapping of hudud punishments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule of tadakhul in hudud, identify which offenses merge, and distinguish the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Repeated identical hadd offenses merge into one punishment because the purpose is achieved; different offenses require separate hadd.

The Hanafi school applies the principle of tadakhul (overlapping) to hudud punishments: if a person commits multiple offenses of the same type (e.g., several qadhf acts), only one hadd is executed. This is because the deterrent and purifying purpose of the punishment is achieved once. However, if the offenses are of different categories (e.g., zina and qadhf), separate hadd are required since each serves a distinct purpose. This lesson explores the rule, its rationale, and the contrasting Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
What is being ruled upon? The passage discusses repeated offenses of qadhf, zina, and drinking. The ruling: one hadd suffices for repeated identical offenses.
This is the Hanafi position.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is rational (talil) based on the purposes (maqasid) of each hadd and the principle of tadakhul. No specific textual evidence is cited; the reasoning is that the purpose of the hadd (deterrence, protection) is achieved by a single punishment.
The Hanafi school uses istihsan and maqasid here.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The legal link: Because the purpose (e.g., protecting honor for qadhf, lineage for zina, intellect for drinking) is attained by one hadd, repeating the same offense does not require a new punishment. If the purposes differ, no overlap occurs.
Each hadd category has a distinct maqsad.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i restricts tadakhul: for qadhf, it applies only when multiple persons are accused with one word, or when same person is accused of the same zina again. Otherwise, each qadhf requires a separate hadd.
The passage quotes Shafi'i's view explicitly.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
The Hanafi school adopts the broader view: all identical offenses merge. This is based on the overarching principle that punishments are meant to serve a purpose, and once achieved, repetition is unnecessary.
The mufta bihi is one hadd for repeated same-type offenses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قذف مراراً رجلاً واحداً أو متعدداً. (ط، عيني) فهو لكله: أي الحد الذي حد به المجرم يكون لكل قذف مراراً ولكل زنا مراراً ولكل شرب مراراً لحصول المقصود وللتداخل في العقوبات بخلاف ما إذا زنى وقذف وشرب حيث يحد لكل واحد على حدة؛ لعدم حصول المقصود بالبعض؛ لاختلاف الأسباب والأغراض، فإن المقصود من حد الزنا صيانة الأنساب ومن حد القذف صيانة الأعراض ومن حد الشرب صيانة العقول فلا يحصل بكل جنس إلا ما قصد لشرعه ولا يوالي بين الحدود خيفة الهلاك، بل ينتظر حتى يبرأ من الأول. فعلى هذا لو جلد للقذف إلا سوطاً ثم قذف آخر في المجلس، فإنه يتم الأول، ولا شيء عليه للثاني للتداخل. ولو ضرب للزنا أو للشرب بعض الحد فهرب ثم زنى أو شرب ثانياً حد حداً مستأنفاً، وقال الشافعي له: إن حد القذف لا يتداخل إلا إذا قذف جماعة بكلمة واحدة أو قذف واحداً بزنا، ثم قذفه بزنا آخر، لا يتداخل الحد بل يجب لكل قذف حد. رمز الحقائق: ۳۹۷/۱] (فتح)
And whoever qadhf repeatedly, one man or multiple. (Tahawi, Ayni) So it is all for him: meaning the hadd with which the criminal is punished suffices for every repeated qadhf, and for every repeated zina, and for every repeated drinking, because the purpose is achieved and because punishments overlap. Contrary to if he committed zina, qadhf, and drinking, then he is hadded for each separately because the purpose is not achieved partially due to different causes and objectives. Indeed, the purpose of zina hadd is to protect lineages, of qadhf hadd to protect honor, and of drinking hadd to protect intellects. So each type achieves only what is intended for its legislation. And they are not carried out consecutively for fear of death, rather one waits until he recovers from the first. Based on this, if he was lashed for qadhf except one lash, then qadhf again in the same gathering, then he completes the first and nothing is upon him for the second due to overlap. And if he was beaten for zina or drinking partly, then fled, then committed zina or drinking a second time, he is hadded a fresh hadd. Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The hadd of qadhf does not overlap except if he qadhf a group with one word, or qadhf one person for zina, then qadhf him for another zina, the hadd does not overlap; rather a hadd is wajib for each qadhf. Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/397] (Fath)
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage explains the rule of overlapping (tadakhul) in hudud punishments within the Hanafi school. The principle: repeated offenses of the same type (e.g., multiple acts of qadhf, or multiple acts of zina) result in a single hadd because the purpose of punishment (deterrence and purification) is achieved by one punishment. However, different types of offenses (e.g., qadhf and zina) require separate hadd because they serve distinct purposes: lineage, honor, intellect. Also, the punishments are not executed consecutively if it would endanger life; one waits for recovery between different hudud. The passage gives two examples: if someone is flogged for qadhf and only one lash remains, then qadhf again, he completes the first and nothing for the second. But if he is partially flogged for zina, then escapes, then commits zina again, he begins a fresh hadd because the first was incomplete. The Shafi'i view is quoted: they do not allow tadakhul for qadhf except when multiple women are accused with one statement, or multiple accusations against the same person for the same act. The Hanafi position is broader: all identical offenses merge into one hadd. The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is that tadakhul applies within the same category of offense.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadakhul): The principle that multiple identical offenses result in a single hadd punishment because the purpose is achieved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a person commits multiple acts of qadhf against different people?
A) He receives a separate hadd for each act.
B) He receives one hadd for all qadhf acts.
C) He receives ta'zir instead of hadd.
D) He is exempt from punishment.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of tadakhul consolidates repeated same-type hadd offenses into a single punishment, preserving the purpose of the penalty while avoiding excessive harm.

Effect of Hadd al-Qadhf on Testimony of the Qadhif
Ruling on rejection of testimony after qadhf hadd, with distinction between Muslim, dhimmi, and slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on testimony for a Muslim, a dhimmi, and a slave who have received hadd al-qadhf, and apply the Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
A Muslim qadhif's testimony is permanently rejected, even after repentance, based on the explicit Quranic command.

This passage addresses the legal consequence of the hadd punishment for false accusation of adultery (qadhf) on the offender's capacity to testify in court. The Quran provides a clear directive, but the application differs based on the witness's status at the time of punishment. We will examine three distinct cases: a free Muslim, a dhimmi, and a slave, and understand the underlying principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage distinguishes three categories: a free Muslim, a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen), and a slave. For each, note the ruling on their testimony after receiving hadd al-qadhf.
The slave case includes a change in status (emancipation) after the punishment.
2
Analyze the ruling for the Muslim
Determine whether repentance affects the testimony. The Quranic verse (24:4) is cited: 'And never accept their testimony forever.' Understand that this makes the rejection permanent.
Emphasis on 'never' (abadan) indicates perpetuity.
3
Analyze the ruling for the dhimmi
The dhimmi loses testimony only concerning other dhimmis. If he converts to Islam after the hadd, his testimony becomes fully acceptable. Understand the reasoning: he acquires testimony capacity through Islam.
Conversion is a fresh start; the hadd's effect does not carry over.
4
Analyze the ruling for the slave
The slave's testimony is permanently rejected, even after emancipation. Note that emancipation does not restore testimony, unlike the dhimmi's conversion.
The slave's inferior status at the time of hadd results in permanent disability.
5
Apply the Quranic evidence
Link each ruling to the Quranic verse or to the principle of capacity acquisition. The verse directly supports the Muslim's permanent rejection. The dhimmi's case uses a different rationale (istihsan or qiyas).
No istihsan needed for the Muslim case; the dalil is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إذا حد المسلم في قذف تسقط شهادته وإن تاب؛ لأن رد شهادته من تمام حده؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً أَبَداً (النور: ٤) وإذا حد الكافر في قذف لم تجز شهادته على أهل الذمة، فإن أسلم قبلت شهادته عليهم وعلى المسلمين؛ لأن هذه الشهادة استفادها بالإسلام فكانت غير مردودة، والعبد إذا حد في قذف ثم عتق لم تقبل شهادته. (مستخلص، فتح)
Then, if a Muslim is hadded for qadhf, his testimony falls, even if he repents, because the rejection of his testimony is part of the completion of his hadd, due to His statement: 'And never accept their testimony forever' (Surat al-Nur, 4). And if a kafir (dhimmi) is hadded for qadhf, his testimony is not permissible against the people of the dhimma. If he becomes Muslim, his testimony is accepted regarding them and regarding Muslims, because he acquired this testimony (capacity) through Islam, so it is not rejected. And a slave, if he is hadded for qadhf, then is emancipated, his testimony is not accepted. (Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage lays out the consequences of hadd al-qadhf on the judicial testimony (shahada) of the person who was punished. The ruling has three parts: (1) A free Muslim who receives hadd al-qadhf loses his testimony permanently, even if he repents, because the Quran (24:4) explicitly commands that their testimony never be accepted. This is an integral part of the punishment. (2) A dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen) who receives hadd al-qadhf loses his testimony only concerning other dhimmis. However, if he converts to Islam after the hadd, he regains his right to testify entirely (both against Muslims and dhimmis). The reasoning is that the capacity to testify is acquired through Islam, and his acceptance of Islam makes him a new person, so the rejection is not carried over. (3) A slave who receives hadd al-qadhf and later gains freedom still has no testimony accepted; the effect of the slave's inferior status combined with the hadd results in permanent rejection. This ruling is consistent with the general principle that a convicted qadhif is considered unreliable in testimony. The relied-upon ruling is as stated.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Judicial testimony given in court by a qualified witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) His testimony is accepted only against dhimmis.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim qadhif's testimony is permanently invalid; a dhimmi's is partially restricted but restored upon conversion; a slave's is permanently invalid even after emancipation.

Ta'zir: Definition, Methods, and Classification
Definition, methods, and general rulings of discretionary punishment (ta'zir)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ta'zir, list its methods, and apply the four-tier classification based on the offender's social status.

Core Idea
Ta'zir is a discretionary, non-fixed punishment left to the judge's discretion, graded by the offender's social rank.

After discussing fixed hudud punishments, this section turns to ta'zir (discretionary punishment). Ta'zir is any deterrent less than a hadd, imposed for major sins without fixed penalties. Its methods, classification, and procedural rules are detailed below.

Guided Path
1
Define ta'zir linguistically and legally
Understand that ta'zir derives from 'azr meaning repulsion/deterrence. Legally, it is discipline less than the hadd.
The passage explicitly states this definition.
2
Understand its obligation and scope
Ta'zir is wajib (obligatory) for any major sin (kabira) that does not have a fixed hadd. This is by consensus of the ummah.
The passage cites al-Ayni for this consensus.
3
Enumerate the methods of ta'zir
Methods include imprisonment, exile, slapping, ear-twisting, harsh speech, beating, and even a stern look. Abu Yusuf also permitted taking wealth.
No fixed measure; judge chooses based on circumstances.
4
Explain the four-tier classification
Ta'zir is graded by the offender's social status: (1) nobles (scholars, Alawis) – only public notification; (2) princes/landowners – notification + court summons; (3) middle class (market people) – also imprisonment; (4) low class – all previous plus beating.
This classification preserves dignity while ensuring deterrence.
5
Note evidentiary and procedural rules
Ta'zir is proven by testimony of two men or one man and two women. Pardon is valid, and it applies to minors (as discipline) and may involve a surety (kafala). Special case: killing if catching zina with spouse/mahram (from al-Munyah).
These rules align with rights of subjects (huquq al-'ibad).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التعزير أي في بيان أحكامه ومن قذف مملوكاً أو كافراً بالزنا، أو مسلما بيا فاسق، أي أو قذف مسلما بقوله فصل في التعزير لما ذكر الحدود، وهي الزواجر المقدرة شرع في زواجر غير مقدرة، والتعزير من العزر بمعنى الرد والردع، وهو التأديب لغة وشرعاً: التأديب دون الحد، وقال العيني وأجمعت الأمة على وجوب التعزير في كبيرة لا توجب الحد، ثم هو قد يكون بالحبس، وقد يكون بالنفي وقد يكون بالصفع يعني الضرب على القفا بالكف، وقد يكون بتعريك الأذن، وقد يكون بالكلام العنيف وقد يكون بالضرب، وقد يكون بنظر القاضي إليه بوجه عبوس، وليس فيه شيء مقدر، وإنما هو مفوض إلى رأي الإمام على ما تقتضي جناياتهم. وقيل: التعزير على أربع مراتب تعزير أشرف :الأشراف وهم العلماء والعلوية يكون بالإعلام فقط بأن يقول القاضي له بالإعلان: بلغني أنك تفعل كذا فلا تفعل، وتعزير الأمراء والدهاقين يكون بالإعلام والجر إلى باب القاضي والخصومة في ذلك، وتعزير الأوساط وهم السوقية بالإعلام والجر والحبس وتعزير الأخساء يكون بهذا كله والضرب، وعن أبي يوسف أن التعزير بأخذ الأموال جائز ،للإمام، وفي "المنية": رأى رجلاً مع امرأته يزني بها أو مع محرمه، وهما مطاوعان قتل الرجل والمرأة جميعاً. ويثبت التعزير بشهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين؛ لأنه من جنس حقوق العباد، ولهذا يقبل فيه الشهادة على الشهادة، ويصح العفو عنه، وشرع في حق الصبيان والتكفيل. [رمز الحقائق: ۳۹۷/۱] (فتح)
Section on ta'zir: meaning in explaining its rulings. And whoever qadhf a slave or a kafir with zina, or a Muslim with 'ya fasiq', meaning or qadhf a Muslim with his saying... Section on ta'zir: because when he mentioned the hudud, which are the fixed deterrents, he began on deterrents that are not fixed. Ta'zir is derived from 'azr meaning repulsion and deterrence, and it is discipline (ta'dib) linguistically and in shari'ah: discipline less than the hadd. Al-Ayni said: The ummah is united on the obligation of ta'zir for a major sin that does not necessitate the hadd. Then it may be by imprisonment, by exile, by slapping (meaning hitting the back of the neck with the palm), by twisting the ear, by harsh speech, by beating, or by the judge looking at him with a frowning face. There is no fixed amount; it is delegated to the opinion of the imam according to what their crimes require. It is said: Ta'zir is of four levels: ta'zir of the nobles (the scholars and 'Alawis) is only by notification (the judge says publicly: I have heard that you do such-and-such, do not do it). Ta'zir of the princes and landowners is by notification and summoning to the court and litigation in that. Ta'zir of the middle class (the market people) is by notification, summoning, and imprisonment. Ta'zir of the base people is by all of that and beating. From Abu Yusuf: ta'zir by taking wealth is permissible for the imam. In al-Munyah: If a man sees his wife committing zina or with his mahram and both are compliant, he may kill both the man and the woman. Ta'zir is established by the testimony of two men or one man and two women, because it is of the category of the rights of the subjects; therefore, testimony upon testimony is accepted in it, and pardon is valid, and it is prescribed for minors and for taking a surety. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/397] (Fath)
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage introduces the section on ta'zir (discretionary punishment). After discussing fixed hudud, the author moves to non-fixed deterrents. Ta'zir is linguistically and legally defined as discipline less than the hadd. The ummah agrees on its obligation for major sins that do not have a fixed hadd. The forms of ta'zir vary: imprisonment, exile, slapping, ear-twisting, harsh words, beating, or even a stern look from the judge. There is no prescribed measure; it is left to the judge's discretion based on the crime and the criminal's status. The passage outlines a four-tier classification of ta'zir based on the social rank of the criminal: for scholars and nobles, public notification; for princes and leaders, notification and being brought to court; for middle-class (traders), also imprisonment; for low-class, all including beating. Abu Yusuf permitted taking wealth as ta'zir. A special case from al-Munyah: a man who catches his wife or mahram committing zina voluntarily may kill both. The proof for ta'zir is established by two male witnesses or one male and two females, as it involves rights of subjects. Thus, testimony upon testimony is valid, pardon is allowed, and it is applicable to minors and can involve surety (kafala). The relied-upon ruling is that ta'zir is left to the judge's discretion, with the above gradations.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zir): A discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd or kaffara; less severe than hadd.
حد (hadd): A fixed, divinely ordained punishment for specific crimes (e.g., zina, theft, drinking wine).
كبيرة (kabira): A major sin that incurs punishment in the Hereafter; here, the trigger for ta'zir if no hadd applies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the highest form of ta'zir for a scholar who commits a major sin without fixed hadd?
A) Public notification by the judge.
B) Imprisonment.
C) Beating.
D) Exile.

Key Takeaway
Ta'zir is a flexible, non-fixed punishment, with method determined by the judge according to the crime and the criminal's status.

Ta'zir for Qadhf of Non-Muhsan Victim
Ruling statement on ta'zir for qadhf of non-muhsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for qadhf of a slave or kafir and identify the conditions of muhsan that trigger hadd vs. ta'zir.

Core Idea
Hadd of qadhf requires a muhsan victim (free, Muslim, chaste); otherwise ta'zir applies.

This lesson examines a ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq that clarifies when qadhf (false accusation of zina) results in the fixed hadd punishment versus discretionary ta'zir. The key is the status of the victim: if the victim is a slave or a kafir, they are not muhsan, and the accuser is punished with ta'zir. The passage also extends ta'zir to other insults that attach shame, such as calling someone a fasiq or kafir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and victim
The act is qadhf (accusation of zina). The victims here are slaves (mamluk) and kafirs. Note that 'slave' includes both fully and partially owned.
The passage uses 'mamlukan mutlaqan' (slave absolutely).
2
Determine the punishment
The punishment is ta'zir (discretionary discipline), not hadd al-qadhf. The reason given: the victim is not muhsan.
Hadd al-qadhf is 80 lashes for a free Muslim muhsan.
3
Understand the condition of muhsan
Muhsan for qadhf requires freedom and Islam. Slaves lack freedom; kafirs lack Islam. Therefore they are not muhsan, so no hadd.
A free Muslim who has been convicted of zina is also not muhsan for qadhf.
4
Expand to similar insults
The passage mentions that other degrading terms like 'fasiq', 'kafir', 'mukhannath' (effeminate) also result in ta'zir because they attach shame (shayn).
All such insults are treated analogously, though not explicit qadhf.
5
Understand the legal principle
There is no room for qiyas in hudud. Thus even if the insult is not explicit zina, ta'zir is legislated as a deterrent.
Ta'zir is wajib to deter corruption and protect honor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قذف مملوكاً أو كافراً بالزنا: مملوكاً مطلقاً سواء كان الملك كاملاً أو ناقصاً. (مستخلص) بالزنا بأن قال: يا زاني أو زنيت أو نحوهما. (عيني) يعزر قاذف المملوك والكافر إذا قذفهما بصريح الزنا، ولا يحد حد القذف؛ لأنهما ليسا بمحصنين؛ لفقد الحرية والإسلام، وأما إذا قال المسلم يا فاسق يا كافر إلى آخر ما ذكر، فإنه يعزر ; لأنه ألحق الشين به، ولا مدخل للقياس في الحدود، فوجب التعزير أي التأديب دون الحد، وقد روي أنه عليها عزر رجلاً قال لغيره: يا مخنث، وغير المخنث . الألفاظ من ملحق به؛ لأنها في معناه في إلحاق الشين؛ ولأن زجر أهل الفساد عن الجنايات واجب تقليلاً لها، والتعزير يصلح زاجراً فيكون مشروعاً. ثم قوله: "عزر" يحتمل وجهين أحدهما أن يكون جواب الشرط؛ لأن قوله: "من قذف" موصولة يتضمن معنى الشرط، والثاني: أن يكون خبر مبتدأ باعتبار أن الموصول مع صلته مبتدأ. (مستخلص، وفتح)
And whoever qadhf a slave or a kafir with zina: a slave absolutely, whether the ownership is complete or incomplete. (Mustakhlas) With zina by saying: 'O zani' or 'you committed zina' or similar. (Ayni) He is subject to ta'zir, the qadhif of a slave and a kafir if he qadhf them with explicit zina, and he is not hadded with the hadd of qadhf because they are not muhsan, due to the lack of freedom and Islam. And if a Muslim says 'O fasiq, O kafir' and the like, he is subject to ta'zir because he has attached shame to him, and there is no room for qiyas in hudud, so ta'zir is wajib, meaning discipline less than the hadd. It is narrated that he (the judge) ta'zir a man who said to another: 'O effeminate' and the like. These words are annexed to it because they are in its meaning in attaching shame. And because deterring the people of corruption from crimes is wajib to minimize them, and ta'zir serves as a deterrent, so it is legislated. Then his saying: 'he ta'zir' admits two possibilities: one is that it is the answer to the condition, because his saying 'whoever qadhf' is a relative clause implying a condition; the second is that it is the predicate of a subject considering that the relative with its clause is the subject. (Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage specifies that qadhf (accusation of zina) against a slave or a kafir, even if using explicit words like 'O zani', does not carry the hadd punishment but instead requires ta'zir (discretionary punishment). The reason is that the victim lacks muhsan status: slaves lack freedom, and kuffar lack Islam. Both are conditions for being muhsan. Thus, the qadhif is not liable for the fixed hadd but is punished with ta'zir. The passage also discusses other insulting words like 'O fasiq', 'O kafir', 'O effeminate' etc. These also result in ta'zir because they attach shame. There is no qiyas in hudud, so even though these insults are not explicit zina accusations, they still call for discipline. The text also gives a grammatical analysis of the word 'عزر' (ta'zir). The relied-upon ruling is consistent: the qadhif of a non-muhsan receives ta'zir.

Key Terms
محصن (muhsan): In the context of qadhf, a person who is free, Muslim, and chaste (not previously convicted of zina). Slaves and kafirs are not muhsan.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment determined by the judge for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd or that do not meet the conditions for hadd.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina against a chaste person. In this passage, the act of accusing someone of zina or similar degrading remarks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) No punishment

Key Takeaway
Hadd al-qadhf applies only when the victim is muhsan (free, Muslim, chaste); otherwise, the accuser is punished with ta'zir.

Ta'zir for Insulting a Muslim with 'Ya Fasiq' and Related Terms
Ruling on ta'zir for calling someone 'ya fasiq'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on ta'zir for calling someone 'ya fasiq' and identify the condition that exempts the speaker from punishment.

Core Idea
Ta'zir for insulting a Muslim with 'ya fasiq' is only wajib if the accusation is false.

This lesson clarifies that insulting a Muslim by calling him a sinner (fasiq) or similar terms incurs a ta'zir punishment, but not the severe hadd of qadhf. The ruling hinges on whether the description is true. We will dissect the conditions and scope of this ruling, and also learn the precise meaning of 'fasiq' versus 'fajir'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
We are dealing with a statement (calling someone 'ya fasiq') that is an insult but not an explicit accusation of zina. Determine whether this falls under qadhf (hadd) or ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
The text explicitly says these are from the category of insult (shatm), and qadhf is applied figuratively.
2
State the ruling and its hukm level
What is the consequence of uttering such an insult? The text says 'fih al-ta'zir' – ta'zir is wajib. Identify that this is a discretionary punishment, not a fixed hadd.
Wajib in Hanafi fiqh: obligatory, but less than fard.
3
Identify the condition for ta'zir
The passage states that ta'zir is given only 'if the one accused is not actually characterized (by that quality)'. If the person is truly a fasiq, no ta'zir because the speaker is truthful.
Truthfulness is a complete defence against ta'zir for slander-like insults.
4
Scope: does it apply to dhimmis?
The text explicitly extends the ruling: 'the one accused is the same whether Muslim or dhimmi'. Note that ta'zir protects honour regardless of faith.
In Hanafi fiqh, dhimmis are protected from false accusations.
5
Distinguish between fasiq and fajir
The passage defines fasiq as one who commits a type of sin, and fajir as one who commits every sin. This distinction matters when assessing whether the insult is true or false.
If the victim is a fajir, calling him a fasiq would be technically true (since fasiq is more general).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو مسلما بيا فاسق: [هو المباشر نوعاً من المعصية أو يا ابن الفاسق. (ط، فتح)] هذه الألفاظ من قبيل الشتم، فإطلاق القذف عليها مجاز ،شرعي، واقتصر المصنف في مسائل الشتم على النداء وليس بقيد؛ لأن الأخبار كذلك كما إذا قال المسلم: أنت فاسق أو فلان فاسق ففيه التعزير أيضاً، وإنما يعزر بهذه الألفاظ إذا لم يكن المقذوف متصفاً لا يعزر؛ لأنه صادق في الأخبار والمقذوف سواء كان مسلماً أو ذمياً الحكم كذلك، والفرق بين الفسق والفجور : أن الفاسق أعم وهو المرتكب نوعاً من المعاصي والفاجر من يرتكب كل معصية. (فتح) فإن كان متصفاً كما يعزر بها،
Or a Muslim with 'ya fasiq': [he is one who commits a type of sin, or 'ya ibn al-fasiq' (Tahawi, Fath)] These words are of the type of insult, so applying the term qadhf to them is figurative, legally. The author confined in the matters of insult to the call (vocation) and it is not a restriction, because the reports are like that, as if a Muslim says: 'You are a fasiq' or 'So-and-so is a fasiq', then ta'zir is also obligatory. He is only ta'zir with these words if the one accused is not actually characterized (by that quality); otherwise he is not ta'zir because he is truthful in his report. And the one accused is the same whether Muslim or dhimmi; the ruling is likewise. The difference between fisq and fujur: that the fasiq is more general, he is one who commits a type of sin, while the fajir is one who commits every sin. (Fath) So if he is characterized (by that), he is ta'zir with them.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage clarifies that using insulting words like 'O sinful one' (ya fasiq) against a Muslim incurs ta'zir, but not the hadd of qadhf, because these words are not explicit accusations of zina. The term 'qadhf' is applied to them metaphorically. The author notes that the examples given (ya fasiq, ya ibn al-fasiq) are not restrictive; any similar insult that attaches shame warrants ta'zir. Importantly, if the person being insulted actually possesses the attribute (e.g., he is truly a known sinner), then the speaker is not punished because he is truthful. This applies whether the victim is Muslim or dhimmi. The text also distinguishes between fasiq (general sinner) and fajir (one who commits every sin). The relied-upon ruling: ta'zir is for insulting a Muslim with demeaning words that do not amount to qadhf.

Key Terms
فاسق (fasiq): One who commits a type of sin (general sinner).
فاجر (fajir): One who commits every sin (more extreme than fasiq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Definition and Obligation of Taʿzīr
Opens the chapter on taʿzīr with definition and proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of taʿzīr, explain that its obligation is established by ijma, and list the discretionary methods of taʿzīr.

Core Idea
Taʿzīr is wajib for major sins without fixed ḥadd, established by ijma, and its method is discretionary.

This lesson introduces taʿzīr as the discretionary punishment for offenses that do not carry a fixed ḥadd. You will learn its linguistic and technical definition, the consensus that makes it obligatory (wajib), and the range of methods a judge may employ—from a stern look to imprisonment. Understanding taʿzīr’s legal basis is essential for distinguishing it from ḥadd punishments.

Guided Path
1
Define taʿzīr linguistically and technically
Identify how the author derives taʿzīr from 'ʿazr' (turning back) and defines it as 'disciplining without the ḥadd'.
The definition is key: taʿzīr is less than ḥadd.
2
Identify the proof that taʿzīr is obligatory
Find the statement of ijma' (consensus) reported by al-ʿAynī: 'The ummah is unanimous on the obligation of taʿzīr for any major sin that does not necessitate a ḥadd.' Note that this makes taʿzīr wajib, not fard.
Ijma is zanni al-thubut but qat'i al-dalala in the Hanafi school.
3
List the discretionary methods of taʿzīr
Enumerate the methods mentioned: imprisonment, exile, slapping, ear-rubbing, harsh speech, beating, and a frowning look. Observe that no method is predetermined.
The judge chooses based on the crime and offender.
4
Understand why taʿzīr is not a fixed punishment
Note the statement: 'ليس فيه شيء مقدر، وإنما هو مفوض إلى رأي الإمام' (nothing is predetermined; it is delegated to the judge's opinion).
This distinguishes taʿzīr from ḥadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التعزير أي في بيان أحكامه ومن قذف مملوكاً أو كافراً بالزنا، أو مسلما بيا فاسق، أي أو قذف • أي أو قذف مسلما بقوله فصل في التعزير لما ذكر الحدود، وهي الزواجر المقدرة شرع في زواجر غير مقدرة، والتعزير من العزر بمعنى الرد والردع، وهو التأديب لغة وشرعاً: التأديب دون الحد، وقال العيني وأجمعت الأمة على وجوب التعزير في كبيرة لا توجب الحد، ثم هو قد يكون بالحبس، وقد يكون بالنفي وقد يكون بالصفع يعني الضرب على القفا بالكف، وقد يكون بتعريك الأذن، وقد يكون بالكلام العنيف وقد يكون بالضرب، وقد يكون بنظر القاضي إليه بوجه عبوس، وليس فيه شيء مقدر، وإنما هو مفوض إلى رأي الإمام على ما تقتضي جناياتهم. وقيل: التعزير على أربع مراتب تعزير أشرف :الأشراف وهم العلماء والعلوية يكون بالإعلام فقط بأن يقول القاضي له بالإعلان: بلغني أنك تفعل كذا فلا تفعل، وتعزير الأمراء والدهاقين يكون بالإعلام والجر إلى باب القاضي والخصومة في ذلك، وتعزير الأوساط وهم السوقية بالإعلام والجر والحبس وتعزير الأخساء يكون بهذا كله والضرب، وعن أبي يوسف أن التعزير بأخذ الأموال جائز ،للإمام، وفي "المنية": رأى رجلاً مع امرأته يزني بها أو مع محرمه، وهما مطاوعان قتل الرجل والمرأة جميعاً. ويثبت التعزير بشهادة رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين؛ لأنه من جنس حقوق العباد، ولهذا يقبل فيه الشهادة على الشهادة، ويصح العفو عنه، وشرع في حق الصبيان والتكفيل. [رمز الحقائق: ۳۹۷/۱] (فتح) مملوكاً مطلقاً سواء كان الملك كاملاً أو ناقصاً. (مستخلص) بالزنا بأن قال: يا زاني أو زنيت أو نحوهما. (عيني) أو مسلماً: عطف على مملوكا" أي أو قذف مسلماً بهذه الألفاظ من "يا فاسق" إلى "يا حرام" زاده، يعزر " قاذف المملوك والكافر إذا قذفهما بصريح الزنا، ولا يحد حد القذف؛ لأنهما ليسا بمحصنين؛ لفقد الحرية والإسلام، وأما إذا قال المسلم يا فاسق يا كافر إلى آخر ما ذكر، فإنه يعزر ؛ لأنه ألحق الشين به، ولا مدخل للقياس في الحدود، فوجب التعزير أي التأديب دون الحد، وقد روي أنه عليها عزر رجلاً قال لغيره: يا مخنث، وغير المخنث . الألفاظ من ملحق به؛ لأنها في معناه في إلحاق الشين؛ ولأن زجر أهل الفساد عن الجنايات واجب تقليلاً لها، والتعزير يصلح زاجراً فيكون مشروعاً. ثم قوله: "عزر" يحتمل وجهين أحدهما أن يكون جواب الشرط؛ لأن قوله: "من قذف" موصولة يتضمن معنى الشرط، والثاني: أن يكون خبر مبتدأ باعتبار أن الموصول مع صلته مبتدأ. (مستخلص، وفتح)
Chapter on Taʿzīr: i.e., explanation of its rulings. Whoever accuses a slave or a disbeliever of fornication, or a Muslim by saying 'O sinner'... The chapter on taʿzīr: when he mentioned the fixed punishments (ḥudūd), which are determined deterrents, he proceeded to non-determined deterrents. Taʿzīr is derived from 'ʿazr' meaning turning back and repelling, and it is disciplining linguistically and legally: disciplining without the ḥadd. Al-ʿAynī said: The ummah is unanimous on the obligation of taʿzīr for a major sin that does not necessitate a ḥadd. Then it may be by imprisonment, by exile, by slapping (i.e., striking the nape with the palm), by rubbing the ear, by harsh speech, by beating, or by the judge looking at him with a frowning face. There is nothing predetermined in it; it is delegated to the judge's opinion according to what their crimes require. It is said: Taʿzīr has four levels: the taʿzīr of nobles (scholars and sayyids) is by merely informing – the judge says to him publicly: 'I heard that you do such and such, so do not do it.' Taʿzīr of princes and chiefs is by informing, dragging to the judge's door, and litigation therein. Taʿzīr of the middle class (market people) is by informing, dragging, and imprisonment. Taʿzīr of the lower class is by all of that plus beating. From Abu Yusuf: taʿzīr by taking wealth is permissible for the ruler. In al-Munya: If a man sees his wife or his female relative committing adultery and both are consenting, he kills both the man and the woman. Taʿzīr is established by the testimony of two men or one man and two women, because it is from the category of rights of people, therefore testimony upon testimony is accepted, and pardon is valid, and it is legislated for minors and bailment. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/397] (Fath) 'A slave' absolutely, whether ownership is complete or incomplete. (Mustakhlas) 'By fornication' i.e., by saying 'O fornicator' or 'you fornicated' or similar. (ʿAynī) 'Or a Muslim': conjuncted to 'slave', i.e., if he accuses a Muslim with these words from 'O sinner' to 'O illegitimate' he is taʿzīr'd. The one who accuses a slave or disbeliever of explicit fornication is taʿzīr'd, not ḥadd, because they are not muḥṣan (chaste) due to lack of freedom and Islam. As for when a Muslim says 'O sinner, O disbeliever' etc., he is taʿzīr'd because he caused him shame, and qiyās has no entry in ḥudūd, so taʿzīr (i.e., discipline without ḥadd) is obligatory. It is narrated that he (upon him) taʿzīr'd a man who said to another 'O effeminate' and the effeminate was not [actually] effeminate. These words are attached to it because they are similar in causing shame, and because deterring people of corruption from crimes is obligatory to reduce them, and taʿzīr serves as a deterrent so it is legislated. Then his saying 'he taʿzīr'd' has two possibilities: one is that it is the answer of the conditional, because the relative clause 'whoever accuses' contains a conditional meaning; the second is that it is a predicate of a subject, considering that the relative clause with its clause is a subject. (Mustakhlas and Fath)
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on taʿzīr from Kanz al-Daqāʾiq. It is a definition-and-ruling passage. The author first defines taʿzīr linguistically and technically: it is a disciplinary punishment less than the fixed ḥadd. He then reports the ijmaʿ (consensus) of the ummah on the obligation of taʿzīr for any major sin that does not carry a fixed ḥadd. This is important: the obligation is wajib, not fard, because the proof is consensus (zannī al-thubūt) rather than a definitive text. Next, the passage enumerates the various methods of taʿzīr: imprisonment, exile, slapping, ear-rubbing, harsh speech, beating, and even a stern look. All are discretionary. The text then mentions a classification of taʿzīr according to the social status of the offender: for nobles, mere notification suffices; for princes, dragging to court; for middle class, added imprisonment; for lower class, added beating. This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on proportionality. A key point: Abu Yusuf’s opinion that taʿzīr by taking wealth is permissible—this is a minority view within the school. The passage then discusses evidence: taʿzīr is established by two men or one man and two women because it is a right of people (ḥuqūq al-ʿibād), unlike ḥadd where the standard is higher. The text then applies the general rule to specific cases: accusing a slave or disbeliever of explicit fornication taʿzīr, not ḥadd, because they lack iḥṣān. Accusing a Muslim with insulting terms (like yā fāsiq) also taʿzīr, because it causes shame and qiyās does not apply to ḥudūd. A prophetic precedent is cited: the Prophet taʿzīr'd a man who called another 'yā mukhanath' (effeminate). The passage ends with grammatical analysis of the word 'ʿazzara' showing its function in the conditional construction.

Key Terms
التعزير (al-taʿzīr): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed ḥadd; it is less than the ḥadd and varies according to the crime and the status of the offender.
الحد (al-ḥadd): Fixed, predetermined corporal punishment for specific offenses (e.g., fornication, theft).
الإجماع (al-ijmāʿ): Consensus of the mujtahid scholars of the ummah on a legal ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidentiary basis for the obligation of taʿzīr according to the passage?
A) A Quranic verse
B) A mutawatir hadith
C) Consensus (ijma) of the ummah
D) Analogical reasoning (qiyas)

Key Takeaway
Taʿzīr is an obligatory (wajib) discretionary punishment for major sins without a fixed ḥadd, proven by ijma.
