The Maximum of Ta'zir: 39 Lashes — Dalil and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Proof for maximum ta'zir and intra-Hanafi disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maximum ta'zir punishment (39 lashes) and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding its derivation.

Core Idea
Ta'zir must remain below the minimum hadd; Abu Hanifa set the maximum at 39 by decreasing one from the slave's hadd of 40.

In this lesson, we examine the proof for the maximum ta'zir punishment in the Hanafi school. The source text presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa (and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Abu Yusuf, who analogized to the free person's hadd instead. We will trace the dalil from the hadith and understand the methodological principles at play.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and its basis
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani: maximum ta'zir is 39 lashes. Note that they based this on the minimum hadd, which is the hadd of a slave for qadhf (40 lashes).
A slave's hadd for qadhf is 40 lashes in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's alternative positions and reasoning
Abu Yusuf proposed 79 lashes (qiyas on free person's hadd of 80 minus one) or 73 lashes (based on an athar from 'Ali). He considered the free person's hadd as the minimum.
Zufar supported Abu Yusuf's qiyas.
3
Locate the dalil: the hadith
The principle is derived from the hadith: 'Whoever reaches a hadd in other than a hadd is from the transgressors.' This prohibits making ta'zir reach a prescribed hadd.
The hadith is cited without a chain; it is well-known among fuqaha.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'بلوغ حد' (reaching a hadd) indicates that ta'zir must be strictly less than the smallest prescribed hadd. Since the smallest hadd is the slave's hadd of 40, the maximum is 39.
This is the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under the mufta bihi, a judge cannot exceed 39 lashes; under Abu Yusuf's view, he could go up to 79 lashes.
The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من تسعة وثلاثون: الأن حد العبيد أقله أربعون فنقص عنه بسوط (ط)] عند الطرفين، وعند أبي يوسف: تسعة وسبعون سوطاً، وعنه ثلاثة وسبعون وعنه أنه يقرب كل جنس إلى جنسه فيقرب اللمس والقبلة من حد الزنا، والقذف لغير المحصن أو للمحصن بغير الزنا من حد القذف صريحاً، وعنه أن التعزير يعتبر على قدر عظم الجرم وصغره، فأبو يوسف اعتبر أدنى الحد في الأحرار، ثم نقص سوطاً في رواية، وهو القياس، وهو قول زفر، وخمسة في أخرى، وهو مأثور عن علي الله فقلده، وهما نظرا إلى أدنى الحد، وهو حد العبد في القذف، وهو وعند مالك: لا حد له، ويفوض إلى الحاكم وعند الشافعي وأحمد: في العبد تسعة سوطاً، أربعون، فنقصا منه سو عشر. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٩٩/١] والأصل فيه قوله عليه: "من بلغ حداً في غير حد فهو من المعتدين، نقل بتخفيف بلغ من البلوغ، وجرى على ألسنة الفقهاء من التبليغ أي من بلغ التعزير حداً فهو من المعتدين، فهما نظرا إلى أدنى الحد، وهو نظر إلى أقل الحد في الأحرار. (مستخلص)
From thirty-nine: Now the hadd of slaves, its minimum is forty, so he decreased one lash from it. (?) According to both parties. According to Abu Yusuf: seventy-nine lashes, and from him seventy-three, and from him that he approximates each type to its own type: he approximates touching and kissing to the hadd of zina, and qadhf of a non-muhsan or of a muhsan with other than zina to the hadd of plain qadhf. And from him that ta‘zir is considered according to the magnitude of the crime and its smallness. So Abu Yusuf considered the minimum hadd for free persons, then decreased one lash in one narration (that is qiyas, and it is the view of Zufar), and five in another narration, which is reported from ‘Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), so he followed him. They both (i.e., Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?) looked to the minimum hadd, which is the hadd of a slave in qadhf, which is... And according to Malik: no limit for it, and it is delegated to the judge. And according to al-Shafi‘i and Ahmad: for a slave, nine? lashes? forty, they decreased a tenth from it. [Ramz al-Haqa’iq: 399/1] The principle for it is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever reaches a hadd in other than a hadd is from the transgressors.' Transmitted with tashdid of bā' from bāligh? It is common on the tongues of fuqaha' from tablīgh, i.e., whoever makes ta‘zir reach a hadd is from the transgressors. So they both looked to the minimum hadd, and he looked to the minimum hadd for free persons. (Mukhtalif)
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
The commentary here elaborates on the maximum of ta‘zīr. The author explains the reasoning behind the limit of 39 lashes. The key point is that ta‘zīr must remain below the minimum hadd punishment. The minimum hadd for a slave in qadhf (false accusation of fornication) is 40 lashes, so ta‘zīr is set at 39. Abu Yusuf, however, analogizes to the minimum hadd of a free person (80 lashes for qadhf) and reduces by one or five, giving 79 or 73. The text mentions that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) considered the slave’s hadd, while Abu Yusuf considered the free person’s hadd but decreased one to follow qiyas or five based on a report from ‘Ali. The hadith 'Whoever raises a punishment to a hadd in non-hadd matters is a transgressor' is cited as a principle. The passage also notes different views of other schools: Malik leaves it to the judge; Shafi‘i and Ahmad fix 40 for a slave but decrease a tenth (i.e., 36? unclear). The commentary ends by reiterating that the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) looked at the minimum hadd (40) and decreased one, while Abu Yusuf looked at the minimum of free persons (80) and decreased.

Key Terms
الحد (al-ḥadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by the Qur’an or Sunnah for specific crimes (e.g., zina, qadhf).
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of fornication or adultery, the hadd for which is 80 lashes for a free person and 40 for a slave.
تعزير (ta‘zīr): Discretionary punishment for crimes not covered by hadd or qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Hadd of drinking (40 lashes)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maximum ta‘zir of 39 lashes is derived from the principle that ta‘zir must be below the minimum hadd, which is the slave’s hadd of qadhf (40 lashes).

Minimum Ta'zir and Permissibility of Imprisonment
States the minimum lashes and rules for adding imprisonment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum ta'zir lashes and explain when imprisonment may be added.

Core Idea
Ta'zir is flexible; the judge sets punishment based on benefit and may combine lashes with imprisonment for the corrupt.

Ta'zir is a discretionary punishment for offenses without fixed hadd. This passage establishes its minimum lashes and clarifies when imprisonment can supplement flogging. Understanding the judge's discretion is key to applying ta'zir correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the minimum ta'zir lashes
Note the text explicitly states the minimum is three lashes. This is a guideline, not a rigid limit.
2
Recognize the judge's discretion
The text says 'no meaning to specifying it when the purpose is achieved without it' – the judge may choose more or even less if beneficial.
3
Find the proof for imprisonment
The Prophet (peace be upon him) imprisoned a man for ta'zir, establishing that imprisonment is valid either alone or combined with lashes.
4
Identify the condition for imprisonment
The text restricts combined punishment to the foolish and corrupt, when beating alone does not achieve the objective.
5
Note the subsidiary ruling on death
If a person dies from hadd or ta'zir, no blood money is due – the punishment is justified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأقله ثلاثة، وصح حبسه بعد الضرب، وأشدّ الضرب التعزير ثم حد الزنا ثم حدّ أي حبس المعزر الشرب ثم حد القذف. ومن حدّ أو عزّر فمات فدمه هدر . لثبوته بإجماع الصحابة أدنى من بأمر الإمام وأقله ثلاثة: أي أقل التعزير ثلاث جلدات ويختلف ذلك باختلاف الأشخاص، فلا معنى لتقديره مع حصول المقصود بدونه، فيكون مفوضاً إلى رأي القاضي بقدر ما يرى المصلحة فيه وعليه المشايخ لله، وهو قول الثلاثة. رمز الحقائق: ٤٠٠/١] حبسه أي وإن رأى الإمام أن يضم الحبس إلى الضرب في التعزير جاز، وقد وصح صح أن النبي عليه حبس رجلا للتعزير، فإذا جاز الاكتفاء به جاز أن يضم إليه والحبس صالح للتعزير؛ لأن من أتهم بوجوب التعزير لا يحبس إلى وقت الثبوت، ومن اتهم بوجوب الحد يحبس إلى وقت ثبوت الحد؛ لأن التعزير الحد، فناسب أن يعاقب به عند التهمة بما يوجب الحد، ولأنه قد لا يحصل الغرض بذلك القدر من الضرب فيجوز حبسه بعد الضرب. (عيني، مستخلص) بعد الضرب إذا كان فيه مصلحة، وصح القيد في السفهاء وأهل الفساد. (معدن ، ع)
And its minimum is three, and his imprisonment is valid after beating. And the severest beating is ta‘zīr, then the hadd of zina, then the hadd of drinking, then the hadd of qadhf. And whoever is punished by hadd or ta‘zīr and dies, his blood is wasted. Its establishment by consensus of the Companions is lower than by order of the Imam. And its minimum is three: meaning the minimum of ta‘zīr is three lashes. And it differs according to persons, so there is no meaning to specifying it when the purpose is achieved without it. So it is delegated to the opinion of the judge to the extent he sees of benefit. And upon this are the mashāyikh, and it is the saying of the three. [Ramz al-Haqā’iq: 400/1] Imprisonment: Meaning if the Imam sees fit to combine imprisonment with beating in ta‘zīr, it is permissible. And it is established (ṣaḥḥa) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) imprisoned a man for ta‘zīr. So if it is permissible to suffice with it, it is permissible to combine it. And imprisonment is suitable for ta‘zīr because one accused of warranting ta‘zīr is not imprisoned until proof, but one accused of warranting a hadd is imprisoned until proof; because ta‘zīr is a less severe punishment, so it is appropriate to punish with it upon accusation for what warrants a hadd? And because the purpose may not be achieved with that amount of beating, so his imprisonment after beating is allowed. (‘Aynī, Mukhtalif) After beating if there is benefit. And the restriction is valid for the foolish and the corrupt. (Ma‘din, ‘A)
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage addresses the minimum of ta‘zīr and the permissibility of adding imprisonment. It states the minimum is three lashes, but this is not a fixed limit; rather it is left to the judge’s discretion. The principle is that ta‘zīr is flexible according to the person and situation. The proof that imprisonment can be added to beating is the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who imprisoned a man for ta‘zīr. The commentator explains that imprisonment is suitable because ta‘zīr is less than a hadd, and it can be used when beating alone does not achieve the objective. However, the restriction is that this combination should be applied to foolish and corrupt people, not to others. The text also mentions that the minimum is 'three' but that is a guideline from the consensus of the Companions? The phrase 'لثبوته بإجماع الصحابة أدنى من بأمر الإمام' is unclear but likely means that the lower limit is established by the consensus of the Companions, but the judge may determine a lesser amount if beneficial.

Key Terms
الحبس (al-ḥabs): Imprisonment as a ta'zir punishment, either alone or combined with lashes.

Severity Comparison of Beatings and Death from Punishment
Ranks severity of beatings and rules on death during punishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ranking of punishment beatings and the reasoning behind it, and explain the ruling that blood is wasted if death occurs during lawful punishment, contrasting it with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Ta'zir beating is the most severe in description; death during lawful punishment is hadar because wajib does not guarantee safety.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two important aspects of Islamic criminal law: the comparative severity of beatings in different punishments and the legal consequences if the punished person dies. The Hanafi school ranks ta'zir as the most intense beating in description, then hadd of zina, then hadd of drinking, then hadd of false accusation. Additionally, if a person dies during a lawful hadd or ta'zir, the Hanafi view is that no compensation is due because the imam was performing an obligation. This contrasts with the Shafi'i school, which requires blood money from the treasury.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ranking order and basis for ta'zir's severity
Locate the sequence: ta'zir, zina, shurb, qadhf. Understand that ta'zir is most severe in description because its number is lenient; to maintain deterrence, the beating must be intense and may be concentrated on one limb.
The text states 'وأشدّ الضرب التعزير' and explains 'لأنه جرى فيه التخفيف من حيث العدد، فلا يخفف من حيث الوصف'.
2
Understand the hadd rankings and their reasoning
Zina is second due to greater crime and Quranic prescription; shurb is third because evidence is certain (observation/smell); qadhf is least because the accuser might be truthful and the punishment already includes rejection of testimony.
For qadhf: 'لأن سببه يحتمل جواز صدق القاذف'
3
Note the differing views of Malik and Ahmad
Malik considers all beatings equal; Ahmad orders zina, then qadhf, then shurb, then ta'zir, or holds zina more severe than ta'zir.
These are valid ikhtilaf within the Ummah.
4
State the Hanafi ruling on death during punishment and its proof
The text rules 'فدمه هدر' (blood is wasted). Proof: establishing punishment is wajib, and wajib does not coexist with liability. The one commanded is not liable for unintended consequences, like a butcher or cupper within normal bounds.
The analogy: 'كالفساد والبزاغ إذا لم يتجاوز المعتاد'
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Shafi'i holds that death is a mistake by the imam, so blood money is due from the treasury. The Hanafi rebuttal is that the imam is performing an obligation, not a mistake.
This difference has practical implications for state liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشدّ الضرب التعزير ثم حد الزنا ثم حد الشرب ثم حد القذف. ومن حدّ أو عزّر فمات فدمه هدر . لثبوته بالكتاب لثبوته بإجماع الصحابة أدنى من بأمر الإمام أشد الضرب التعزير: يعني الشدة في الضرب يكون في التعزير، وقيل: المراد بأشد الضرب جمع الأسواط في عضو واحد يكون في التعزير؛ لأنه جرى فيه التخفيف من حيث العدد، فلا يخفف من حيث الوصف، كي لا يؤدي إلى فوات المقصود، وهو الانزجار، ويتقي المواضع التي تتقى في الحدود وعن أبي يوسف أنه يضرب فيه الظهر والألية فقط. وذكر في حدود الأصل يفرق التعزير على الأعضاء فيما إذا بلغ أقصى غاية الحد، وأما في التعزير الذي لا يبلغ إلى أقصى غايته مثل ثلاثة أسواط أو أربعة أو خمسة فلا يفرق؛ لأنه خفف فيه باعتبار العدد. (مستخلص، عيني) ثم حد الزنا أي بعد التعزير أشد الضرب حد الزنا؛ لأنه ثابت بالكتاب والعدد؛ ولأن جنايته أعظم حيث شرع فيه الرجم وقوله ثم حد الشرب أي بعد حد الزنا أشد الضرب حد الشرب؛ لأن جناية الشرب مقطوع بها بمشاهدة الشرب والاحضار إلى الحاكم بالرائحة. (معدن، مستخلص) ثم حد القذف الضعف سببه لاحتمال صدق القاذف. (ط)] أي بعد حد الشرب أشد الضرب حد القذف؛ لأن سببه يحتمل جواز صدق القاذف، وقد جرى فيه التغليظ من حيث رد الشهادة فنزلت منزلة قطع لسانه، فلا يغلظ من حيث الوصف بل يخفف وعند مالك الكل سواء، وقال أحمد : أشد الضرب حد الزنا ثم القذف ثم الشرب ثم التعزير، وعن أحمد حد الزنا أشد من التعزير. رمز الحقائق ٤٠٠/١٥] (معدن، مستخلص) قدمه هدر أي باطل لا يجب به شيء على أحد ؛ لأن إقامة الحد والتعزير من الواجبات، والواجب لا يجامع الضمان؛ لأن المأمور فعل ما أمر به وفعل المأمور لا يتقيد بالسلامة كالفساد والبزاغ إذا لم يتجاوز المعتاد. وقال الشافعي: تجب الدية في بيت المال؛ لأنه إذا مات يكون خطأ من الإمام فضمان خطئه فيما يقيمه من الأحكام في بيت المال. رمز الحقائق: ٤٠٠/١] (فتح)
And the most severe beating is ta‘zīr, then the hadd of zina, then the hadd of drinking, then the hadd of qadhf. And whoever is punished by hadd or ta‘zīr and dies, his blood is wasted. Its establishment by the Book? Its establishment by consensus of the Companions is lower than by order of the Imam? The most severe beating is ta‘zīr: meaning the severity in beating is in ta‘zīr. And it is said: the meaning of 'most severe beating' is gathering the lashes on one limb in ta‘zīr, because leniency has been applied in terms of number, so it should not be lenient in terms of description, so that the purpose (deterrence) is not lost. And one avoids the places that are avoided in hadd punishments. According to Abu Yusuf, he beats only the back and the buttocks. And it is mentioned in Hudūd al-Asl that ta‘zīr is distributed over the limbs when it reaches the utmost limit (40?); but in ta‘zīr that does not reach its utmost limit, like three, four, or five lashes, it is not distributed because leniency has been applied in number. (Mukhtalif, ‘Aynī) Then the hadd of zina: i.e., after ta‘zīr, the most severe beating is the hadd of zina, because it is established by the Book and the number? And because its crime is greater since stoning is legislated in it. Then the hadd of drinking: i.e., after the hadd of zina, the most severe beating is the hadd of drinking, because the crime of drinking is certain by observing the drinking and bringing to the judge by smell. (Ma‘din, Mukhtalif) Then the hadd of qadhf: weakness? its cause due to the possibility that the accuser is truthful. (?) i.e., after the hadd of drinking, the most severe beating is the hadd of qadhf, because its cause may allow the possibility that the accuser is truthful, and severity has been applied in terms of rejecting testimony, so it is treated like cutting his tongue, so it is not made severe in description but rather lenient. According to Malik, all are equal. Ahmad said: the most severe beating is the hadd of zina, then qadhf, then drinking, then ta‘zīr. And from Ahmad: the hadd of zina is more severe than ta‘zīr. (Ramz al-Haqā’iq 400/15) (Ma‘din, Mukhtalif) He presented it (i.e., the ruling that blood is wasted): Meaning it is invalid, nothing is obligatory on anyone. Because establishing hadd and ta‘zīr is an obligation, and obligation does not coexist with compensation. Because the one commanded did what he was commanded, and the action of the one commanded is not conditioned on safety, like [the examples of] a butcher and a cupper if they do not exceed the norm. Al-Shāfi‘ī said: The blood money is obligated from the treasury, because if he dies, it is a mistake by the imam, and the guarantee of his mistake concerning what he enforces of rulings is from the treasury. (Ramz al-Haqā’iq: 400/1) (Fatḥ)
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage covers two topics: the ranking of severity of beatings among different punishments, and the ruling on death resulting from punishment. The Hanafi position is that ta‘zīr beating is the most severe in description (though least in number), because it aims at deterrence without the constraints of hadd. The order of severity is: ta‘zīr, then hadd of zina, then hadd of drinking, then hadd of qadhf. This is based on the nature of the crime and the type of evidence required. In contrast, Malik holds all equal; Ahmad has a different order. The second ruling is that if a person dies during a lawful hadd or ta‘zīr punishment, no compensation (blood money) is due to the deceased's family because the imam was performing an obligation. The Hanafi school argues that the obligation does not guarantee safety. Imam Shafi‘i, however, holds that the blood money should be paid from the public treasury (bayt al-māl) because it is considered a mistake by the imam, and the guarantee for his mistakes lies with the treasury.

Key Terms
هدر (hadar): Wasted; blood for which no compensation (diyah or qisas) is due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person dies during a lawful ta'zir beating, what is required from the imam?
A) Blood money from the imam's personal wealth
B) Blood money from the treasury
C) No compensation (blood is wasted)
D) Qisas

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies punishment beatings with ta'zir as most severe in description, and holds that death during lawful punishment is hadar (wasted) because the obligation to punish exempts from liability.

Rulings of Ta'zir: Minimum, Severity Order, and Liability for Death
Exposition of ta'zir rules: minimum strikes, imprisonment, severity order, and liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on ta'zir's minimum punishment, its severity relative to hadd punishments, and the liability (or lack thereof) for death resulting from lawful punishment, and distinguish the Hanafi position from that of Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Ta'zir's minimum is three lashes; its blows are most severe in description but light in number; death during lawful punishment incurs no liability.

Ta'zir is a discretionary punishment for crimes without fixed hadd. The Hanafi school establishes its rulings from Quran and consensus, detailing the judge's discretion, the combination of imprisonment, and the ranking of severity among punishments. This lesson unpacks the key rules and the debated liability for death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
What does the matn say about ta'zir? Identify the minimum lashes, the permissibility of imprisonment, the order of severity, and the ruling on death.
The matn is the starting point; each clause has a ruling.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites Quran and Ijma as proof for ta'zir itself, and a hadith for imprisonment. Identify these proofs.
The main dalil for ta'zir is the Quran (general commands to punish) and consensus of the Companions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each proof establish the ruling? For the minimum, it is based on practice of the Companions; for imprisonment, the Prophet's action; for severity order, the relative gravity of crimes.
The link between proof and ruling is not always direct; some rulings are deduced by the scholars.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text presents the Shafi'i view on liability for death. State both positions and their proofs.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Why does the Hanafi school hold that no blood money is due? Because the execution of hadd/ta'zir is a wajib act, and the commanded person does not guarantee safety.
The tarjih is based on the principle of 'al-ma'mur la yadman'.

كتاب الحدود
بيان أحكام التعزير
لثبوته بالكتاب
وأقله ثلاثة، وصح حبسه بعد الضرب، وأشدّ الضرب التعزير ثم حد الزنا ثم حد الشرب ثم حد القذف. ومن حدّ أو عزّر فمات فدمه هدر.
لثبوته بإجماع الصحابة
أدنى من بأمر الإمام
وأقله ثلاثة: أي أقل التعزير ثلاث جلدات ويختلف ذلك باختلاف الأشخاص، فلا معنى لتقديره مع حصول المقصود بدونه، فيكون مفوضاً إلى رأي القاضي بقدر ما يرى المصلحة فيه وعليه المشايخ لله، وهو قول الثلاثة. رمز الحقائق: ٤٠٠/١] حبسه أي وإن رأى الإمام أن يضم الحبس إلى الضرب في التعزير جاز، وقد صح أن النبي عليه حبس رجلا للتعزير، فإذا جاز الاكتفاء به جاز أن يضم إليه والحبس صالح للتعزير؛ لأن من أتهم بوجوب التعزير لا يحبس إلى وقت الثبوت، ومن اتهم بوجوب الحد يحبس إلى وقت ثبوت الحد؛ لأن التعزير دون الحد، فناسب أن يعاقب به عند التهمة بما يوجب الحد، ولأنه قد لا يحصل الغرض بذلك القدر من الضرب فيجوز حبسه بعد الضرب. (عيني، مستخلص) بعد الضرب إذا كان فيه مصلحة، وصح القيد في السفهاء وأهل الفساد. (معدن ، ع) أشد الضرب التعزير: يعني الشدة في الضرب يكون في التعزير، وقيل: المراد بأشد الضرب جمع الأسواط في عضو واحد يكون في التعزير؛ لأنه جرى فيه التخفيف من حيث العدد، فلا يخفف من حيث الوصف، كي لا يؤدي إلى فوات المقصود، وهو الانزجار، ويتقي المواضع التي تتقى في الحدود وعن أبي يوسف أنه يضرب فيه الظهر والألية فقط. وذكر في حدود الأصل يفرق التعزير على الأعضاء فيما إذا بلغ أقصى غاية الحد، وأما في التعزير الذي لا يبلغ إلى أقصى غايته مثل ثلاثة أسواط أو أربعة أو خمسة فلا يفرق؛ لأنه خفف فيه باعتبار العدد. (مستخلص، عيني) ثم حد الزنا أي بعد التعزير أشد الضرب حد الزنا؛ لأنه ثابت بالكتاب والعدد؛ ولأن جنايته أعظم حيث شرع فيه الرجم وقوله ثم حد الشرب أي بعد حد الزنا أشد الضرب حد الشرب؛ لأن جناية الشرب مقطوع بها بمشاهدة الشرب والاحضار إلى الحاكم بالرائحة. (معدن، مستخلص)
ثم حد القذف الضعف سببه لاحتمال صدق القاذف. (ط) أي بعد حد الشرب أشد الضرب حد القذف؛ لأن سببه يحتمل جواز صدق القاذف، وقد جرى فيه التغليظ من حيث رد الشهادة فنزلت منزلة قطع لسانه، فلا يغلظ من حيث الوصف بل يخفف وعند مالك الكل سواء، وقال أحمد : أشد الضرب حد الزنا ثم القذف ثم الشرب ثم التعزير، وعن أحمد حد الزنا أشد من التعزير. رمز الحقائق ٤٠٠/١٥] (معدن، مستخلص) قدمه هدر أي باطل لا يجب به شيء على أحد؛ لأن إقامة الحد والتعزير من الواجبات، والواجب لا يجامع الضمان؛ لأن المأمور فعل ما أمر به وفعل المأمور لا يتقيد بالسلامة كالفساد والبزاغ إذا لم يتجاوز المعتاد. وقال الشافعي: تجب الدية في بيت المال؛ لأنه إذا مات يكون خطأ من الإمام فضمان خطئه فيما يقيمه من الأحكام في بيت المال. رمز الحقائق: ٤٠٠/١] (فتح)
Book of Hudud. Explanation of rulings of ta'zir. It is established by the Book. Its minimum is three, and it is valid to imprison after beating, and the most severe beating is ta'zir, then hadd of zina, then hadd of drinking, then hadd of qadhf. Whoever is hadded or ta'zired and dies, his blood is wasted. It is established by consensus of the companions. Its minimum is three: that is, the least of ta'zir is three lashes, and it varies according to persons, so there is no meaning to specifying it when the purpose is achieved without it, so it is delegated to the opinion of the judge according to what he sees of benefit, and upon this are the mashayikh, and it is the saying of the three. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 1/400) His imprisonment: that is, if the imam sees to combine imprisonment with beating in ta'zir, it is permissible, and it is established that the Prophet (peace be upon him) imprisoned a man for ta'zir. So if it is permissible to suffice with it, it is permissible to combine it, and imprisonment is suitable for ta'zir because one accused of wajib ta'zir is not imprisoned until the time of proof, and one accused of wajib hadd is imprisoned until the time of proof of hadd, because ta'zir is less than hadd, so it is appropriate to punish with it upon accusation with what necessitates hadd, and because the goal may not be achieved with that amount of beating, so imprisonment after beating is permissible. (Ayni, Mustakhlas) After beating if there is benefit, and the restriction is valid for the foolish and corrupt people. (Midan, A.) The most severe beating is ta'zir: that is, severity in beating occurs in ta'zir. And it is said: the meaning of 'most severe beating' is gathering lashes on one limb in ta'zir, because it is lightened in terms of number, so it is not lightened in terms of description, lest it lead to loss of the purpose, which is deterrence, and he avoids the areas that are avoided in hudud. From Abu Yusuf: he strikes the back and buttocks only. And it is mentioned in Hudud al-Asl: ta'zir is distributed over the limbs when it reaches the utmost limit of the hadd. As for ta'zir that does not reach its utmost limit, like three lashes or four or five, it is not distributed, because it is lightened in terms of number. (Mustakhlas, Ayni) Then hadd of zina: that is, after ta'zir, the most severe beating is hadd of zina, because it is established by the Book and number, and because its crime is greater, since stoning is legislated in it. And his saying: then hadd of drinking: that is, after hadd of zina, the most severe beating is hadd of drinking, because the crime of drinking is certain by witnessing drinking and bringing to the judge by smell. (Midan, Mustakhlas) Then hadd of qadhf: its cause is weak due to the possibility of the qadhif being truthful. (T.) That is, after hadd of drinking, the most severe beating is hadd of qadhf, because its cause allows the possibility of the qadhif being truthful, and it has been severely treated in terms of rejecting testimony, so it is akin to cutting his tongue, so it is not made severe in terms of description but rather lightened. According to Malik, all are equal. Ahmad said: the most severe beating is hadd of zina, then qadhf, then drinking, then ta'zir. From Ahmad: hadd of zina is more severe than ta'zir. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 15/400) (Midan, Mustakhlas) He said: his blood is wasted: that is, nothing is obligatory on anyone because establishing hadd and ta'zir is among the obligations, and what is obligatory does not combine with liability, because the commanded person did what he was commanded to do, and the action of the commanded is not restricted to safety, like spoilage and injury when he does not exceed the customary. Al-Shafi'i said: the blood money is obligatory in the treasury, because if he dies, it is a mistake by the imam, and liability for his mistake in what he enforces of judgments is in the treasury. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 1/400) (Fath)
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of al-Quduri (or from Kanz al-Daqa'iq) explaining the rulings of ta'zir (discretionary punishment). It begins by stating that ta'zir is established by the Quran and by consensus of the Companions. The matn declares: 'Its minimum is three, and it is valid to imprison after beating, and the most severe beating is ta'zir, then hadd of zina, then hadd of drinking, then hadd of qadhf. Whoever is hadded or ta'zired and dies, his blood is wasted.' The commentary expands on each clause. First, the minimum ta'zir is three lashes, but the exact number is left to the judge's discretion based on the individual and the need. The judge may also combine imprisonment with beating, as established by the Prophet's practice of imprisoning a man for ta'zir. The reason: the accused of a ta'zir offense is not imprisoned before proof, unlike a hadd offense. Imprisonment is suitable because ta'zir is less than hadd. Then it discusses the severity of beating: ta'zir is the most severe in terms of description (e.g., concentrating lashes on one limb) to ensure deterrence, but it is lightened in number. Abu Yusuf restricts beating to the back and buttocks. The order of severity among punishments is: (1) ta'zir (most severe blows), (2) hadd of zina, (3) hadd of drinking, (4) hadd of qadhf. Hadd of qadhf is lightened because the accuser might be truthful. Contrasts with Malik (all equal) and Ahmad (different order). Finally, if a person dies from hadd or ta'zir, no blood money is due because the execution of a wajib act does not entail liability; the official did what he was commanded. Al-Shafi'i differs, holding that blood money is paid from the treasury because it is a judicial error. The Hanafi position is that such death is 'hadar' (wasted).

Key Terms
التعزير (al-ta'zir): A discretionary punishment given by a judge for crimes that do not have a fixed hadd penalty; its minimum is three lashes but varies by case.
الحد (al-hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Shari'ah (e.g., for zina, drinking, qadhf).
هدر (hadar): Legally wasted; no blood money or compensation is due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The blood money is wajib on the imam's personal wealth.
B) The blood money is paid from the public treasury.
C) No blood money is due; the blood is hadar.
D) The judge must pay compensation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that ta'zir's minimum is three lashes, its beating can be more intense than hadd, and no blood money is due if death occurs from lawful punishment.

Husband's Ta'zir of Wife and Diyah Liability
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'zir and diyah liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five permissible grounds for a husband's ta'zir of his wife, explain the condition of safety that triggers diyah, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding diyah for death from intercourse.

Core Idea
Husband's ta'zir is permissible but conditional on safety; death obligates diyah, unlike intercourse where mahr precludes double compensation.

This lesson examines a nuanced fiqh passage that balances a husband's right to discipline his wife with liability for harm. The author specifies five legitimate reasons for ta'zir, but crucially attaches a condition of safety: if the discipline results in death, diyah (blood-money) is due. The passage then defends the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) that death from intercourse does not incur diyah, against Abu Yusuf's dissent, based on the role of mahr as a guarantee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and conditions of ta'zir
The passage states that a husband may discipline his wife for five specific matters: abandoning lawful adornment, not responding to the call to bed, leaving obligatory prayer, leaving ghusl, and leaving the house without right. This ta'zir is permissible (mubah) but not obligatory, and is restricted by a condition of safety.
The condition of safety means the discipline must not cause death or serious harm.
2
Understand the diyah liability for ta'zir
If the wife dies from the ta'zir, diyah becomes obligatory. The reasoning: since ta'zir is not wajib but mubah, it is subject to safety. If death occurs even from permitted discipline, diyah is due; for unpermitted discipline, it is even more so.
This is a key principle: permission does not eliminate liability for harm caused.
3
Recognize the objection (intercourse case)
An objector raises the case of intercourse: if a husband has intercourse with his wife and she dies (or is injured internally), according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad there is no liability, even though intercourse is permissible and not conditioned with safety. Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing that diyah should be due.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; the opposing school here is Abu Yusuf.
4
Analyze the response defending the majority view
The response argues that diyah is not required because the dower (mahr) already serves as a guarantee for the benefit of the vulva. Imposing diyah would be double compensation for a single benefit, which is invalid. Moreover, the mahr makes the act a commanded one, not merely personal satisfaction.
The key legal concept: one cannot have two guarantees (daman) for the same subject matter.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a wife dies from intercourse, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule no diyah; Abu Yusuf rules diyah is owed. The text defends the majority view, which is the mufta bihi.
This illustrates how a difference in legal reasoning leads to different outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف الزوج إذا عزّر زوجته لترك الزينة، والإجابة إذا دعاها إلى فراشه، وترك الصلاة والغسل والخروج من البيت. أي ولأجل الخروج أي ولترك الإجابة بخلاف الزوج إذا عزر إلخ أي بخلاف الزوج إذا عزر زوجته؛ لأجل هذه الأشياء الخمسة، فماتت الزوجة حيث تجب الدية؛ لأن تعزير الزوجة مباح ليس بواجب، فيتقيد بشرط السلامة والتخصيص بهذه الأشياء ليعلم الحكم في غيرها بالطريق الأولى؛ لأن إذن الشرع في هذه الأشياء موجود في تأديبه إياها، فلو ماتت بالتأديب المشروع وجب الدية، فبالتأديب الغير المأذون أولى أن تحب. فإن قلت: يرد على هذا إذا جامع امرأته فماتت من الجماع أو أفضاها حيث لا ضمان عليه عندهما وإن كان الجماع مباحا ولم يقيداه بشرط السلامة خلافاً لأبي يوسف، قلت: إنما لا يجب لأجل وجوب ضمان المهر في ابتداء الجماع فلو وجبت الدية بموتها كان فيه إيجاب ضمانين بمقابلة مضمون واحد وهو منافع البضع وذلك لا يجوز، ولأنه لما نزل المهر في مقابلة منفعة البضع فصار مأذونا في الانتفاع من جهة الشرع فلم يبق مستوفيا حق نفسه فقط بل كان فعله بأمر الشارع أيضاً. (مستخلص، عيني) لترك الزينة: أي الشرعية وهي قادرة عليها . ( عيني) إلى فراشه وكانت طاهرة من حيض ونفاس. (عيني) وترك الصلاة: أي ولأجل ترك الصلاة المفروضة عيني) والغسل أي وترك الغسل من الجنابة. من البيت بغير حق، فإنه يضمن ديتها لو ماتت. (ط)
Contrary to the husband if he disciplines his wife for leaving adornment, and responding when he calls her to his bed, and leaving prayer, and washing (ghusl), and leaving the house. That is, (he disciplines) for leaving (adornment), for leaving (adornment), and for leaving response. Contrary to the husband if he disciplines, etc., i.e., contrary to the husband if he disciplines his wife for these five matters, and the wife dies, then diyah becomes obligatory because disciplining the wife is permissible (mubah) not obligatory, so it is restricted to the condition of safety and specification to these matters to inform the ruling in other matters by way of primary reasoning; because the permission of the Lawgiver in these matters exists in his disciplining her. So if she dies from the permitted discipline, diyah is obligatory, so by unpermitted discipline it is more likely that it becomes obligatory. If you say: This is refuted by the case when he has intercourse with his wife and she dies from the intercourse or he injures her internally, where there is no liability (daman) upon him according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) even though intercourse is permissible and they did not restrict it with a condition of safety, contrary to Abu Yusuf. I say: It is not obligatory (diyah) only because of the obligation of the dower (mahr) in the beginning of intercourse; if diyah were obligatory upon her death, it would entail two guarantees in exchange for one guaranteed thing, namely the benefits of the vulva, and that is not permissible. And because when the dower is established in exchange for the benefit of the vulva, the use becomes permitted by the Lawgiver, so he is not merely satisfying his own right but his act is also by command of the Lawgiver. (Mukhtalas, 'Ayni) 'For leaving adornment': i.e., the lawful adornment while she is capable of it. ('Ayni) 'To his bed': while she is pure from menstruation and postpartum bleeding. ('Ayni) 'And leaving prayer': i.e., for leaving the obligatory prayer. ('Ayni) 'And washing': i.e., for leaving ghusl from janaba. 'Leaving the house': without right, then he guarantees her diyah if she dies. (T)
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the husband's ta'zir (discretionary punishment) of his wife and the diyah (blood-money) liability if death results. The author first states the ruling: a husband may discipline his wife for five specific matters—abandoning lawful adornment, not responding to his call to bed, leaving prayer, leaving ghusl, and leaving the house without right. This disciplining is permissible (mubah) but not obligatory, so it is restricted by a condition of safety: if the disciplining causes death, diyah is due. The restriction to these five matters implies that for other matters, the ruling is applied with more reason—if diyah is due for permitted discipline, it is even more so for unpermitted discipline. The objection raised is about the case of intercourse: if a man has intercourse with his wife and she dies, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), there is no liability even though intercourse is permissible and they did not condition safety, contrary to Abu Yusuf. The response explains that in intercourse, the dower (mahr) is already a guarantee for the benefit of the vulva; imposing diyah would be double compensation for one benefit, which is invalid. Additionally, the mahr makes the intercourse a commanded act, not merely personal satisfaction. The passages ends with glosses on each of the five matters. The overall point: the husband's ta'zir carries potential diyah liability, while death from intercourse does not (according to the majority), due to the structural role of mahr.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment less than hadd, here applied by husband to wife for specific matters.
دية (diyah): Blood-money paid to heirs for accidental or quasi-intentional killing.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee; here refers to financial compensation for harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a husband's disciplining of his wife become liable for diyah according to the passage?
A) Only if the disciplining is for an unpermitted matter
B) If it causes death, even if for a permitted matter
C) Only if the disciplining is excessive and unintended
D) Never, because it is a husband's right

Key Takeaway
Husband's ta'zir of wife is permissible for five specific matters but carries diyah liability if death results; death from intercourse does not incur diyah due to mahr covering the benefit.

Definition and Conditions of Sariqa
Defining theft and its conditions for hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sariqa, list the three conditions for the cutting penalty, and explain the nisab dispute with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools.

Core Idea
No cutting for theft unless the thief is mukallaf, takes 10 dirhams secretly, and from a hirz.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of legal theft (sariqa) for the purpose of the fixed penalty (hadd) of amputation. The passage distinguishes between the broader linguistic meaning and the narrower legal definition that triggers cutting. You will learn the precise conditions required for the hadd to apply, including the important nuance of secrecy depending on day or night. The lesson also addresses the well-known ikhtilaf (disagreement) over the minimum value (nisab) of the stolen property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition
Extract from the passage the specific legal definition of sariqa that leads to cutting: the taking by a mukallaf of ten dirhams secretly.
Note that the linguistic definition is broader; additional shar'i conditions are added for the hadd.
2
List the conditions for cutting
Identify the three conditions explicitly mentioned: (1) the thief must be mukallaf (sane, adult, speaking, sighted), (2) the taking must be secret (with day/night nuance), (3) the stolen property must reach the nisab of ten dirhams (or one dinar). A fourth condition (hirz) is mentioned as forthcoming.
Each condition is derived from the text's phrasing and the hadith quoted.
3
Analyze the secrecy condition
Understand the two-tier requirement: by day, secrecy must be maintained from beginning to end; by night, only the beginning need be secret. Also note that secrecy is judged by the thief's belief, not the owner's knowledge.
This practical distinction reflects the possibility of help arriving by day.
4
Examine the nisab dispute
Identify the three positions: Hanafi (10 dirhams), Shafi'i (1/4 dinar = 3 dirhams based on shield hadith), and Maliki (3 dirhams). Understand the Hanafi evidence: the hadith 'لا قطع إلا في دينار أو عشرة دراهم' and the companion statement that the shield was worth 10 dirhams.
The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument relies on the authority of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar.
5
Appreciate the wisdom behind the order of hudud
Note the passage's explanation for why the author began with zina, then drinking, then qadhf, then theft: each protects a higher priority (lineage, intellect, honor, wealth).
This reflects the maqasid (higher objectives) of Shari'a.

(عيني)] بفتح السين وكسر الراء، ولك إسكانها مع فتح السين وكسرها، وهي قسمان صغرى وكبرى بدأ بالكلام على الصغرى؛ لكثرتها. وركنها الأخذ، وشرعاً: "أخذ الشيء خفية بغير حق نصاباً كان أو لا" باعتبار الحرمة، وأما باعتبار القطع فما ذكره المصنف، وقدم حد الزنا؛ لأنه شرع لصيانة الأنساب والعرض، وفيه إحياء النفوس؛ لأن الولد من الزنا هالك معنى؛ لعدم من يربيه ثم حد الشرب؛ لأنه لصيانة العقول التي بها قوام النفوس، ثم حد القذف؛ لأنه لصيانة الأعراض، ثم حد السرقة؛ لأنه لصيانة الأموال والأموال وقاية النفس والعقل والعرض، ولهذا أفرده بكتاب على حدة. (فتح) مكلف [ أي عاقل بالغ ناطق بصير، ولو مملوكا أو كافرا. (عيني، ط )] قيد بـ"المكلف" احترازا عن الصبي والمجنون، حتى لو قا لا قطع عليهما؛ لأن العقوبة يستدعي التكليف، وقيد بـ"الخفية" احترازا عن النهب والاختلاس، أي أخذ المكلف من حيث الخفية والاستسرار ابتداء وانتهاء إذا كانت السرقة بالنهار، وابتداء لا غير إذا كانت بالليل، كما إذا نقب الجدار على الاستسرار، وأخذ المال المالك مكابرة جهراً، يقطع أيضاً؛ لأنه من وقت لا يلحقه الغوث فيه، فلو لم يكتف فيه بالخفية ابتداء، لامتنع القطع في أكثر السراق لاسيما في ديار مصر، بخلاف النهار؛ لأنه وقت يلحقه فيه الغوث. وإنما شرط أن يكون خفية على زعم السارق، حتى لو دخل دار إنسان فسرق وأخرجه من الدار ، وصاحب الدار يعلم ذلك، والسارق لا يعلم أنه يعلم قطع، وإن كان يعلم أن صاحب الدار يعلم ذلك لا يقطع؛ لأنه جهر ليس بخفية رمز الحقائق: ٤٠١/١] (مستخلص) عشرة دراهم وزن سبعة مثاقيل، وهي نصاب السرقة. (عيني، ط] لقوله عليه: "لا قطع إلا في دينار أو عشرة دراهم"، . "، فقد زيد شرعاً على المعنى اللغوي أوصاف، منها في السارق وهو كونه مكلفاً، ومنها في المسروق: وهو كونه مالاً متقوماً مقدراً، ومنها في المسروق منه وهو كونه حرزاً كما يأتي بيانها، والمعنى اللغوي – أي الأخذ خفية - مراعى فيها إما ابتداء وانتهاء كما في النهار، أو ابتداء فقط كما في الليل. وزيادة الأوصاف لإناطة القطع؛ إذ لا شك أن أخذ أقل من النصاب خفية سرقة شرعاً باعتبار التحريم والضمان، لكن لم يعلق الشرع به حكم القطع، فنصابها عندنا: عشرة دراهم وعند الشافعي قدر ربع دينار. وعند مالك قدر ثلاثة دراهم؛ لما روي أنه عليه قطع في ثمن مجن، ثمنه ثلاثة دراهم، وفي رواية: قيمته ثلاثة دراهم، رواه الجماعة، غير أن الشافعي قال: كانت قيمة الدينار على عهد النبي عليه اثنى عشر درهماً، والثلاثة ربعها والربع هو المعتبر، فالأخذ بالأقل المتيقن به أولى، قلنا: قال ابن عباس وابن عمر : كانت قيمة المحن الذي قطع فيه رسول الله عشرة دراهم .
Book of Theft: i.e., concerning explanation of its rulings. It is: the taking by a responsible person (mukallaf) secretly of an amount of ten coined dirhams. Theft in the Shari'a: 'secret' in the genitive as an attribute of 'ten'. The child, plunder. Book of Theft: [In language: taking a thing secretly without permission of its owner, whether property or otherwise. ('Ayni)] With the letter sin and kasra on the ra', and you may also pronounce it with sukun on the sin and with fatha and kasra, and it is of two types: minor and major. He began with the minor because it is more frequent. Its pillar is taking. And in Shari'a: 'taking a thing secretly without right, whether it reaches the nisab or not' in terms of prohibition, but in terms of cutting, it is what the author mentioned. He presented the hadd of zina first because it is legislated to protect lineages and honor, and in it is revival of souls because the child of zina is effectively lost due to lack of one who raises him. Then the hadd of drinking because it is to protect intellects by which souls are sustained. Then the hadd of qadhf because it is to protect reputations. Then the hadd of theft because it is to protect wealth, and wealth is a safeguard for soul, intellect, and honor; for this reason he devoted a separate book to it. (Fath) 'Mukallaf': i.e., sane, adult, speaking, sighted, even if slave or disbeliever. ('Ayni, T) He restricted with 'mukallaf' to exclude the child and the insane, so if they (child, insane) take, there is no cutting on them because punishment requires legal responsibility. He restricted with 'secretly' to exclude plunder (nahb) and snatching (ikhtilas). That is, the taking by the mukallaf must be with hiddenness and concealment from beginning to end if the theft is by day, and only at the beginning if by night. For example, if he breaks through a wall secretly and takes the property from the owner forcefully openly, he is also cut because it is a time when help cannot reach him. If he were not satisfied with hiddenness at the beginning, cutting would be prevented for most thieves, especially in the land of Egypt, unlike day because it is a time when help can reach him. And the condition is that it be secret in the estimation of the thief, so that if he enters a person's house, steals, and takes it out of the house, and the owner knows that, but the thief does not know that he knows, then cutting is applied. If he knows that the owner knows, then there is no cutting because it is open, not secret. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/401) (Mukhtalas) Ten dirhams, weight seven mithqals, and it is the nisab of theft. ('Ayni, T) Due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no cutting except in a dinar or ten dirhams.' So, additional attributes have been added in Shari'a to the linguistic meaning: among them, regarding the thief, that he be mukallaf; regarding the stolen object, that it be valuable property of a specified amount; regarding the person from whom it is stolen, that it be in a guarded place (hirz), as will be explained. The linguistic meaning – i.e., taking secretly – is observed either from beginning to end as in day, or only at the beginning as in night. The addition of attributes is for attaching the ruling of cutting; there is no doubt that taking less than the nisab secretly is theft in Shari'a in terms of prohibition and liability, but the Lawgiver did not attach the ruling of cutting to it. So the nisab with us (Hanafis) is ten dirhams, with al-Shafi'i it is a quarter of a dinar, and with Malik it is three dirhams. Because it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) cut for the price of a shield, its price three dirhams, and in a narration: its value three dirhams, narrated by the group. However, al-Shafi'i said: 'The value of the dinar at the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) was twelve dirhams, and three is a quarter of it, and the quarter is considered, so taking the least certain is better.' We (Hanafis) say: Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) said: 'The value of the shield for which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) cut was ten dirhams.'
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on the hadd of theft (sariqa). It begins by defining theft for the purpose of cutting as the secret taking by a mukallaf (legally responsible person) of ten coined dirhams. The author distinguishes between the linguistic and legal definitions, noting that linguistically it is any secret taking, but legally for the cutting penalty, additional conditions are required. The passage explains the wisdom behind the order of hadd punishments: zina first (protecting lineage), then drinking (protecting intellect), then qadhf (protecting honor), then theft (protecting property). The conditions for cutting are then detailed: the thief must be mukallaf (excluding minors and insane), the taking must be secret (excluding open seizure or snatching), and the nisab (minimum value) is ten dirhams. An important nuance is that the requirement of secrecy depends on the time: by day, secrecy must be from inception to completion; by night, only inception need be secret. This practical ruling addresses situations where help can be summoned. Also, secrecy is subjective to the thief's belief. The passage then presents the nisab debate: the Hanafi position of ten dirhams is supported by the hadith 'No cutting except in a dinar or ten dirhams'. The Shafi'i and Maliki positions are given with their evidence, and the Hanafi response relies on the statement of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar that the shield in the hadith was worth ten dirhams. The overall lesson: theft incurs cutting only when strict conditions are met; the nisab dispute is resolved by Hanafi reliance on companion statements.

Key Terms
سرقة (sariqa): The act of taking property secretly without right; for cutting it requires specific conditions.
مكلف (mukallaf): Legally responsible person: sane, adult, speaking, sighted; includes slave and disbeliever.
نصاب (nisab): Minimum value of stolen property required for cutting: ten dirhams (Hanafi).
حرز (hirz): Guarded place where property is kept; a condition for cutting (mentioned here as forthcoming).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires ten dirhams as the nisab for cutting, relying on the hadith and companion statements, distinguishing itself from other schools.

Conditions of Hiraz and Proof of Theft: Confession and Witnesses
Condition of hiraz and rules of proof for hadd theft

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of hiraz for theft, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of confessions required, and apply the procedural rules for witness testimony in hadd cases.

Core Idea
Theft must be proven by confession or two witnesses; one confession suffices per the majority, and the imam must question witnesses thoroughly.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq details two essential elements for applying the hadd of theft: the stolen property must be from a secure place (hiraz), and the proof must be established either by the thief's confession or by the testimony of two male witnesses. Within the Hanafi school, there is a dispute about the number of confessions needed, with Abu Yusuf initially requiring two. The passage also instructs the imam to cross-examine witnesses on details like time, place, and relationship, to ensure no doubt remains.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of hiraz
Identify that security is either by a secure place (like a house, chest) or by a guardian (someone present guarding the goods). Understand that livestock in the open desert or goods in a mosque without the owner are not in hiraz, so no cutting.
The passage emphasises that hiraz is fulfilled by either place or keeper.
2
Determine the modes of proof for the hadd
Theft is proven by the thief's confession or by testimony of two male witnesses. Refusal to testify (nukul) does not lead to cutting, even if the property is guaranteed.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on confession
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that one confession suffices; Abu Yusuf initially required two. Understand their arguments: confession lacks suspicion of lying, unlike testimony, and the analogy to zina is rejected because zina requires four witnesses as an exception.
Bishr narrated that Abu Yusuf retracted to the majority view, making the mufta bihi one confession.
4
Apply the imam's procedural duty when witnesses testify
The imam must question witnesses about the manner (e.g., breaking a wall), nature (e.g., eavesdropping), place (whether from hiraz), time (whether the thief was a minor), and relationship (whether the victim is a relative or spouse). Any doubt prevents the hadd.
The imam also detains the thief until witnesses appear for suspicion.
5
Assess the practical consequences
The mufta bihi is one confession; if the imam finds doubt from witness testimony, the hadd is not applied, and only discretionary punishment (ta'zir) may apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محرزة: [نصب على الحال من العشرة أي محفوظة بالحرز (عيني)] أي حال كون عشرة دراهم محفوظة بالحرز، ولما كان الحرز بشيئين أشار إليهما بقوله: "مكان" وهو الموضع الذي يعدّ لإحراز الأمتعة فيه كالدور والبيوت والصندوق والحانوت ونحوها أو تكون محفوظة بحافظ كمن جلس في الصحراء أو في المسجد أو في الطريق ومعه متاع يحفظه، سواء كان نائماً أو مستيقظاً، أو كان المتاع عنده بحضرته أو تحته، هو الصحيح. رمز الحقائق: ٤٠٢/١] وبهذين القيدين - أي المكان والحافظ - احترز عما إذا سرق المواشي من الصحراء، أو شيئا من المسجد وليس صاحبه عنده حيث لا يقطع. (مستخلص) فيقطع: أي يجب قطع يد السارق إذا أخذ المال بالقيود المذكورة بإقراره مرة واحدة عند الطرفين، وقال أبو يوسف: لا يقطع إلا بإقراره مرتين؛ لأنه حد فيه فيعتبر عدد الإقرار فيه بعدد الشهود كما اعتبر في الزنا، لهما: أن السرقة ظهرت بإقراره مرة فيكفيه كما في القصاص وحد القذف ولا اعتبار بالشهادة؛ لأن الزيادة يفيد فيها تقليل تهمة الكذب، ولا يفيد في الإقرار شيئاً؛ لأنه لا تهمة فيه، واشتراط الزيادة في الزنا بخلاف القياس، فيقتصر على مورده، وذكر بشر رجوع أبي يوسف إلى قولهما. وقوله: أو شهد "رجلان" أي كذلك يجب القطع لو شهد على سرقته رجلان؛ لأنه حد فاختص بشهادة الرجال ليتحقق الظهور كما في سائر الحقوق، ويجب أن يسألهما الإمام عن كيفية السرقة الجواز أنه نقب البيت وأدخل يده فحينئذ لا قطع عليه، وعن ماهيتها؛ لأن من يسمع كلام الغير سراً يسمى سارقاً، قال الله تعالى: ﴿ إِلَّا مَن اسْتَرَقَ السَّمْعَ (الحجر: ۱۸)، ويسأل عن مكانها؛ الجواز أن يكون الأخذ من غير الحرز، ويسأل عن زمان؛ لجواز أن يكون في زمان صباه، ويسأل عن المسروق منه هل هو أجنبي أو قريب من السارق أو زوج، ويحبسه إلى أن الشهود للتهمة، ثم يحكم بالقطع، بخلاف التعزير، ونبه بحصر الحجة في الإقرار والشاهدين على أنه لا يقطع يسأل . عن بالنكول وإن ضمن المال. (مستخلص، فتح عيني) مرة: في قول الأكثر، ومرتين عند أبي يوسف في مجلسين مختلفين. (عيني)
['Muhrazatan' (secure): accusative hal from 'ten' meaning guarded in a secure place. (Ayni)] i.e., the ten dirhams being guarded in a secure place. Since security is by two things, he pointed to them by his saying: 'place', i.e., the location prepared for storing goods, like houses, rooms, chests, shops, and the like; or it is guarded by a keeper, like one who sits in the desert, mosque, or road with his goods which he guards, whether he is sleeping or awake, or the goods are with him present or under him; that is the correct view. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/402) By these two conditions – place and keeper – he excludes the case where livestock are stolen from the desert, or something from a mosque while its owner is not present, where there is no cutting. (Mustakhlas) 'So he is cut': i.e., the hand of the thief must be cut when he takes the property with the mentioned conditions, by his confession once according to both parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and Abu Yusuf said: He is not cut except by his confession twice, because it is a hadd, so the number of confessions is considered by the number of witnesses, as is considered in zina. Their argument (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the theft is established by his confession once, so it suffices as in retaliation and the hadd of slander, and there is no consideration of testimony because increasing it reduces the suspicion of lying, but it does not help in confession because there is no suspicion in it. The requirement of increase in zina is contrary to analogy, so it is confined to its instance. Bishr mentioned that Abu Yusuf returned to their view. And his statement: 'or two men testify' – i.e., likewise cutting is obligatory if two men testify against his theft, because it is a hadd, so it is specific to the testimony of men to achieve clarity as in all other rights. The imam must ask them (the witnesses) about the manner of the theft, lest he had broken the wall and inserted his hand, in which case there is no cutting; and about its nature, because one who listens secretly to others' speech is called a thief – Allah said: 'Except such as steal a hearing' (Quran 15:18); and he asks about its place, lest the taking was not from a secure place; and he asks about its time, lest it was during his childhood; and he asks about the victim, whether he is a stranger, a relative of the thief, or a spouse. He detains him until the presence of [؟] witnesses for suspicion, then he judges the cutting, contrary to discretionary punishment. And he indicated by restricting the proof to confession and two witnesses that he is not cut by refusal (nukul) even if he guarantees the property. (Mustakhlas, Fath, Ayni) 'Once' – according to most; 'twice' according to Abu Yusuf in two different sessions. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage addresses two critical conditions for the hadd of theft: first, that the stolen property must be in a secure place (hiraz), and second, the mode of proof. The security is either by a place (like a locked house or chest) or by a guardian (someone present guarding the goods). If livestock are stolen from the open desert, or something from a mosque without the owner present, no hand-cutting applies. The ruling then discusses the proof: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, a single confession is sufficient; Abu Yusuf initially required two confessions (analogous to zina where four witnesses are required), but later retracted to the majority view. The passage then covers the requirement of two male witnesses for the hadd, and details the imam's duty to question the witnesses thoroughly about the manner, nature, place, time, and relationship of the victim to ensure the hadd is not applied in cases of doubt (like the thief being a minor or the victim being a relative/spouse). Finally, it notes that refusing to testify (nukul) does not lead to cutting, even if the thief guarantees the property.

Key Terms
حرز (hiraz): A secure place (like a house or chest) or the presence of a guardian that protects property from theft.
إقرار (iqrar): Confession; a voluntary admission of guilt. In theft, one confession suffices for the hadd according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).
شهادة (shahada): Testimony; in theft, two male witnesses are required. The imam must question them thoroughly to avoid mistaken application of the hadd.

Conditions for Cutting the Hand in Theft
Explains conditions of nisab, protection, and proof for hadd of theft.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions required for the hadd of theft and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of confessions.

Core Idea
The hand is cut only if the stolen goods are protected, reach the nisab of 10 dirhams, and the theft is proven by one confession or two witnesses.

The hadd punishment for theft is not applied lightly. The Hanafi school sets strict conditions to ensure that the punishment is only applied when there is certainty, avoiding doubt. This lesson breaks down the three essential conditions: the value of the stolen goods (nisab), that they were securely protected (muhriz), and that the theft is proven by confession or testimony. We will also explore a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement about how many confessions are needed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
From the passage, extract the three prerequisites for cutting the hand: nisab (minimum value), muhriz (protected goods), and proof (iqrar or shahada).
2
Understand the nisab determination
The nisab is 10 dirhams minted, based on the value of a shield (mujann) agreed upon by the Companions. The weight is 7 mithqals. If the stolen silver is unminted or of lower value, the hand is not cut.
Value is assessed by two just experts.
3
Define muhriz (protection)
Muhriz means the goods are in a secure place (house, shop, chest) or guarded by a person (even if the owner is asleep). Livestock in open pasture or goods in a mosque without the owner are not muhriz.
This blocks the hadd in many common scenarios.
4
Analyze the proof requirement: confession
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold one confession suffices. Abu Yusuf required two, analogizing to zina. The response: zina is exceptional; confession has no suspicion, so one is enough. Abu Yusuf later retracted.
This is the intra-Hanafi dispute.
5
Analyze the proof requirement: testimony
Two just male witnesses are required. The judge must interrogate them on manner, nature, place, time, and relationship to the victim to ensure all conditions are met. The thief is imprisoned until the witnesses are cleared of suspicion.
Nukul (refusal to swear) does not trigger the hadd.

ف يقطع: أي يجب قطع يد السارق إذا أخذ المال بالقيود المذكورة بإقراره مرة واحدة عند الطرفين، وقال أبو يوسف: لا يقطع إلا بإقراره مرتين؛ لأنه حد فيه فيعتبر عدد الإقرار فيه بعدد الشهود كما اعتبر في الزنا، لهما: أن السرقة ظهرت بإقراره مرة فيكفيه كما في القصاص وحد القذف ولا اعتبار بالشهادة؛ لأن الزيادة يفيد فيها تقليل تهمة الكذب، ولا يفيد في الإقرار شيئاً؛ لأنه لا تهمة فيه، واشتراط الزيادة في الزنا بخلاف القياس، فيقتصر على مورده، وذكر بشر رجوع أبي يوسف إلى قولهما. وقوله: أو شهد "رجلان" أي كذلك يجب القطع لو شهد على سرقته رجلان؛ لأنه حد فاختص بشهادة الرجال ليتحقق الظهور كما في سائر الحقوق، ويجب أن يسألهما الإمام عن كيفية السرقة الجواز أنه نقب البيت وأدخل يده فحينئذ لا قطع عليه، وعن ماهيتها؛ لأن من يسمع كلام الغير سراً يسمى سارقاً، قال الله تعالى: ﴿ إِلَّا مَن اسْتَرَقَ السَّمْعَ (الحجر: ۱۸)، ويسأل عن مكانها؛ الجواز أن يكون الأخذ من غير الحرز، ويسأل عن زمان؛ لجواز أن يكون في زمان صباه، ويسأل عن المسروق منه هل هو أجنبي أو قريب من السارق أو زوج، ويحبسه إلى أن الشهود للتهمة، ثم يحكم بالقطع، بخلاف التعزير، ونبه بحصر الحجة في الإقرار والشاهدين على أنه لا يقطع

مرة: في قول الأكثر، ومرتين عند أبي يوسف في مجلسين مختلفين. (عيني)
The Book of Theft. Rulings of theft. Protected by a place or a guardian, so the hand is cut if he confesses once, or two men testify. Taking voluntarily, not coerced. And since they differed over the value of a shield while agreeing that the nisab is determined by it, we go to the majority for certainty; because no one said that the hand is not cut for ten, and what is less than it is disputed, so cutting is not obligatory due to doubt and caution to ward off the hadd. The standard for these dirhams is the weight of seven mithqals as in zakat. His saying "minted" is an adjective for "ten", indicating that if he steals unminted silver weighing ten or more but its value is less than ten minted, he is not cut. Similarly for silver vessels or counterfeit coins if he steals them and their value is less, or their value is ten but weight less, he is not cut. Value is established by the statement of two just men who have knowledge of values. "Protected" in the accusative as a state of the ten, i.e., being protected in a secure place. Since protection is by two things, he pointed to them by his saying "place" which is a location prepared for securing goods, such as houses, rooms, chests, shops and the like; or it is protected by a guardian, like one who sits in the desert or in the mosque or on the road and has goods with him that he guards, whether asleep or awake, or the goods are with him in his presence or under him; that is the correct view. By these two restrictions—place and guardian—he guards against the case of stealing livestock from the desert or something from the mosque when its owner is not present, where there is no cutting. So the hand is cut: that is, the thief's hand must be cut if he takes the property with the mentioned conditions by his confession once according to the two sides. Abu Yusuf said: He is not cut except by confession twice, because it is a hadd, and the number of confessions is considered equal to the number of witnesses as in zina. Their argument: Theft is established by his confession once, so it suffices as in qisas and the hadd of qadhf, and testimony is not considered; because increasing witnesses reduces suspicion of lying, but it does nothing in confession because there is no suspicion in it. Requiring increase in zina is contrary to analogy, so it is limited to its case. Bishr mentioned that Abu Yusuf retracted to their view. His saying: "or two men testify" means that cutting is also obligatory if two men testify to his theft, because it is a hadd so it is specific to testimony of men to achieve clarity as in other rights. The imam must ask them about the manner of the theft, because it is possible that he broke into the house and inserted his hand, in which case there is no cutting; and about its nature, because one who secretly hears others' speech is called a thief; Allah says: "Except one who steals a hearing" (15:18); and he asks about its place, because it is possible that the taking was not from a secure place; and he asks about its time, because it is possible that it was at a time of his childhood; and he asks about the one stolen from, whether he is a stranger or a relative of the thief or a husband, and he imprisons him until the witnesses are free from suspicion, then he judges cutting, unlike ta'zir. He pointed out that the evidence is limited to confession and two witnesses, indicating that he is not cut by nukul (refusal to swear) even if he guarantees the property. "Once": according to the majority; twice according to Abu Yusuf in two different sessions.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq opens the chapter on theft by stating the core ruling: the hand of a thief is cut if he steals goods that are protected (muhriz) either by being in a secure place or in the presence of a guardian, and if the theft is proven by the thief's confession once or by the testimony of two just men. The commentary then explains each element in detail.

First, the nisab (minimum threshold) is established as ten dirhams, using the historical reference to a shield (mujann) whose value the Companions agreed upon as the nisab. The Hanafi jurists adopt the higher value (ten dirhams) out of caution, since the hadd must be averted by doubt. The weight of these dirhams is seven mithqals, like in zakat. If the stolen silver is unminted or of lower value, the hand is not cut. Value is determined by two just experts.

Next, the commentary defines muhriz: a place prepared for storing goods (like houses or shops) or a guardian (like a person watching goods in the desert). If livestock is stolen from open pasture or goods from a mosque when the owner is absent, the hand is not cut because it is not properly protected.

The text then addresses the proof of theft. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that confession once suffices for cutting. Abu Yusuf initially required two confessions, analogizing to zina, but the response is that zina is exceptional. Since confession carries no suspicion of falsehood, one confession is enough, as in qisas and qadhf. The passage notes that Abu Yusuf later retracted.

For testimony, two male witnesses are required, as in other hadd punishments. The judge must interrogate them thoroughly about the manner (e.g., breaking and entering), nature (hearing secrets?), place (was it from a secure place?), time (was the thief an adult?), and the relationship with the victim. The thief is imprisoned until the witnesses are cleared of suspicion. The hadd is not applied in cases of nukul (refusal to swear) even if the thief guarantees the property.

This passage establishes the strict conditions for the hadd of theft, reflecting the Hanafi principle of averting hudud by doubts.

Key Terms
محرزة (muhriz): Protected; goods stored in a secure place or guarded by a person.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum value (10 dirhams) of stolen goods required for the hadd of theft.
إقرار (iqrar): Confession by the thief admitting to the theft.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position, what is the nisab for the hadd of theft?
A) 1/4 dinar
B) 10 dirhams minted
C) 3 dirhams
D) Any value above zero

Key Takeaway
The hadd of theft is strictly conditioned on nisab, muhriz, and proof; the majority holds one confession suffices.

Joint Theft and the Nisab Requirement: Individual Liability
Ruling on multiple thieves: each must obtain a nisab for the hand to be cut.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on joint theft, apply the individual nisab requirement to multi-thief scenarios, and evaluate the opposing views of Malik, Zufar, and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
In joint theft, each thief must individually obtain a nisab for the hadd to apply; collective liability is rejected.

When multiple thieves act together, the question arises whether the hadd punishment applies to all or only to those who personally meet the conditions. The Hanafi school insists on individual liability: each participant must receive at least a nisab (10 dirhams) from the stolen goods. This lesson unpacks that ruling, contrasts it with the views of Imam Malik and other Hanafi scholars, and demonstrates the practical consequences through real cases.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core Hanafi ruling: each joint thief must individually obtain a nisab (10 dirhams) for the hand to be cut. If any thief receives less than nisab, the hadd is not applied to that individual.
This is the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Identify the opponents and their views
List the opposing positions: Malik (all cut for one nisab by analogy to qisas), Zufar (only the carrier is cut), and Abu Yusuf (exemption if a minor or insane person took the goods).
Zufar and Abu Yusuf are within the Hanafi school.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand each opponent's dalil: Malik uses qiyas on qisas (indivisible life-taking), Zufar focuses on physical removal from the secure place, and Abu Yusuf distinguishes based on capacity (minor/insane).
Malik's argument is the most prominent inter-madhhab challenge.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Study how the Hanafi school rebuts each objection: against Malik, theft is divisible (property) unlike qisas; against Zufar, all participants are involved in the theft; against Abu Yusuf, the majority view holds that sane adults are not excused if a minor participated.
The Hanafi response emphasizes the divisibility of property and the typical division of roles among thieves.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Work out the practical difference: e.g., three thieves steal 30 dirhams and divide equally. Under Hanafi, all are cut; under Malik, all are cut for a different reason; under Zufar, only the carrier; under Abu Yusuf, if a minor took it, adults are not cut.
This shows how different rulings lead to different outcomes in identical scenarios.

قطعوا إلخ: أي إذا اشترك جماعة في سرقة، وأخذ المال بعضهم وقسموه بينهم، فأصاب كل واحد منهم - أي عشرة دراهم - يقطع يد الكل؛ لأن المعتاد بينهم أن يتولى بعضهم الأخذ، ويستعد الباقون للدفع، وإن أصاب لكل أقل من ذلك لا يقطع، وقال مالك: يقطعون بنصاب واحد كالقصاص، قلنا: القصاص يتعلق بسبب لا يتجزأ، وهو إزهاق الروح، فينسب إلى جميعهم بخلاف السرقة وقال :زفر إن الإخراج من الحرز يتحقق من الحامل، فيقتصر القطع عليه. ولو كان فيهم صغير أو مجنون سقط الحد عن الباقين عند الطرفين. وقال أبو يوسف: إن تولى الأخذ الصغير أو المجنون لا يجب عليهم القطع، وإن أخذ الكبار العقلاء وجب. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٠٢/١] نصاب وهو عشرة دراهم ولو لم يصب لكل نصاب لا قطع (عيني)
And the one who takes among them, they are cut if each gets a nisab, and he is not cut for wood... i.e., if the thieves are a group... they are cut etc.: i.e., if a group participates in theft, and some of them take the money and divide it among them, and each one gets a nisab (i.e., ten dirhams), the hand of all is cut; because the usual practice among them is that some take and others prepare to defend. And if each gets less than that, he is not cut. Malik said: They are cut for one nisab, like in qisas. We said: Qisas is related to a cause that is indivisible, which is taking life, so it is attributed to all of them, unlike theft. Zufar said: The removal from the secure place is realized by the carrier, so cutting is limited to him. If there is a minor or insane person among them, the hadd is dropped from the rest according to the two sides. Abu Yusuf said: If the minor or insane person undertook the taking, cutting is not obligatory on them; if the sane adults took it, it is obligatory. Nisab: it is ten dirhams, and if each does not get a nisab, no cutting.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when multiple persons jointly commit theft. The ruling is clear: each thief must individually obtain a nisab (10 dirhams) from the stolen property for the hand to be cut. If they steal a total that when divided gives each less than nisab, no hand is cut. The rationale is that in a group theft, it is common that one physically takes the goods while others stand guard or facilitate; thus all are considered participants in the theft. If each receives a nisab, all are cut.

Imam Malik disagreed, arguing that they should all be cut even if the total is one nisab, by analogy to qisas (retaliation) where if a group kills one person, all are executed. The Hanafi response is that qisas is indivisible because taking life is a single act that cannot be divided; theft, however, is about taking property, which is divisible. Thus each thief's share is considered separately.

Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) argued that only the one who physically removes the goods from the secure place (the carrier) should be cut. The text does not provide a direct response to Zufar but implies the majority view that all participants are cut if each gets nisab.

Further, if a minor or an insane person is among the thieves, the hadd is dropped from the sane adults according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf differentiates: if the minor or insane person actually took the goods, the sane adults are not cut; but if the sane adults took it, they are cut.

This passage illustrates the Hanafi emphasis on individual liability in hudud punishments: the hadd is only applied when the specific conditions are met by each individual.

Key Terms
اشتراك (ishtirak): Participation; here it refers to a group of persons jointly committing theft.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum threshold of stolen goods (10 dirhams) required for the hadd of theft.
حامل (hāmil): Carrier; the person who physically removes the stolen goods from the secure place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All three
B) Only the two who got 10 dirhams each
C) Only the one who got 5 dirhams
D) No one

Key Takeaway
In joint theft, the hadd of cutting the hand applies only to those thieves who individually obtain at least a nisab (10 dirhams) from the stolen property.

Exempt Items from the Hadd of Theft
Ruling with proof listing exempt items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the list of items exempt from the hadd of theft under Hanafi law and explain the proof and rationale for their exemption.

Core Idea
Hadd of theft is averted for trifling or perishable items because doubt and lack of secure protection override the general rule.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq enumerates specific items that are exempt from the hadd (amputation) penalty for theft, even if their value reaches the nisab. The Hanafi school relies on a hadith from Aisha and the principle that trivial or inherently insecure items create a legal doubt (shubha) that blocks the punishment. Understanding these exemptions is crucial for correctly applying Islamic criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list and categories
Note the items: wood, grass, reeds, fish, birds, game, arsenic, red ochre, lime, fresh fruit. They fall into natural, wild, or perishable categories.
2
Locate the primary proof
The hadith of Aisha (reported by al-Daraqutni) states that the hand was not cut for trifling things. This is the central evidence.
The hadith is ahad with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Understand the rationale
The text gives two reasons: these items are not securely stored (wood is left at doors, birds fly), and they are not highly valued. This creates shubha that averts the hadd.
The hand is cut only when all conditions are clear and free from doubt.
4
Note exceptions and distinctions
If wood is worked (teak, ebony) or birds are domestic (chickens, ducks), the ruling may change; some scholars require cutting for domestic birds.
The text says the opinion exempting all birds is more correct.
5
Contrast with other schools
The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools generally cut for any property reaching nisab, except a few items like soil and water. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul.
One narration from Abu Yusuf also aligns with the majority.

Source Text
